Specifically, there’s not a given ritual to be performed or a particular object that will have that effect. Let’s begin by clearing up that little misconception.” “Spe-hih-ic-y?” Grimm inquired.

“Specifically, there are several key targets that must be eliminated by the time they achieve their strategy. The pact is, of course, the agreement between the Kingdom of Lugunica and the Holy Dragon Volcanica. Do you know what it actually stipulates?”

Wilhelm looked at her. “It says that the Dragon will be really nice and help us out anytime the kingdom is in terrible danger, right?”

“Yes-as we’ve seen many times. The kingdom has flourished under the Dragon’s protection. There have been no invasions by other nations, and even natural disasters of which we can hardly conceive have been averted. Just one

little crack has appeared: the Demi-human War.”

That made Wilhelm and the others raise their eyebrows.

“You’ve all thought it, haven’t you? That if the Dragon’s pact were still in effect, then the war would never have happened. That civil war was a wakeup call.” Her eyes swept the carriage, and everyone in it responded with silence.

Wilhelm and Grimm had had the same conversation in Bordeaux’s office some months prior. They had said the same thing that Roswaal was now telling them: The Dragon was not coming. Everyone who had been involved in the civil war knew it or, at least, felt a dim intuition.

And it wasn’t just the people of the kingdom. The Empire knew it, too, as did the Holy Kingdom and the city states. Everyone guessed-but no one had yet made sure.

“Nobody wants to be the first to plunge their hand into a bubbling stew,” Roswaal said. “But supposing that they realized that the pot they thought was on the fire was actually empty?”

“Is that what you think Stride is trying to do?” asked Wilhelm, finally grasping Roswaal’s point.

Stride had stolen the text of the Dragon Tablet, as Jionis had feared. He had tenaciously pursued the Sword Saint Theresia, and he had involved himself in the plotting of the demi-human remnants. He had done all this for the same reason: to crack the shell around the Dragonfriend Kingdom of Lugunica.

If he could prove the pact that both Lugunica and the other realms suspected may not exist anymore, in fact was gone-well, that would indeed be akin to the abolition of the pact with the Holy Dragon.

To demonstrate this, however, Stride and his conspirators would have to achieve something.

“A victory over us… Or, I guess, over the Sword Devil Wilhelm van Astrea. No wonder they asked for you by name. It’s all starting to make sense.” Bordeaux, who had reached the same conclusion, looked at the Sword Devil, who touched the blade at his hip. The sword Veltol had chosen for him. He wanted to feel the Astreas there at his side.

He was angry, yes-angry at being the target of a plot that inconvenienced others on a kingdom-wide scale. But much better this than the alternative that things should transpire somewhere Wilhelm could not reach.

“It doesn’t change what I have to do,” he said. “Cut down Stride and bring an end to all the chaos he’s sowing.”

“Yeah,” Grimm said, immediately nodding.

At that moment, there was no one who could have outdone the two of them in sheer motivation and determination to fight Stride and his faction. He ought to have known he had made enemies of two people who would be fearsome foes.

“Good. That’s good,” Roswaal said, closing her blue eye when she sensed their aura of battle burgeoning. “Incidentally, my good Bordeaux, do you remember what I asked you for before we left? Is the following unit as ready as theycanbe?”

“Mm, damn right they are. But there’s some stuff I’m not so sure about reporting to you on. I won’t go quite so far as to say it could be granting an advantage to the enemy…would you?”

“No, not at all. You’ll see soon.”

No sooner had Roswaal spoken than they did, in fact, see.

The interior of the dragon carriage was thrown into chaos, with much gasping and shouting. They found themselves tossed out of their seats, their weapons-propped nearby-bouncing away, and they could barely keep their feet. That was the shock: A dragon carriage would never normally go runaway like this. The land dragon who pulled the carriage, protected by a wind-repel blessing, should have found no obstacles for its feet. Neither poor roads nor headwinds could interfere with such a beast, and the blessing extended to the carriage the creature drew. Yet somehow, the blessing had been interrupted, throwing the vehicle in which Wilhelm and the others rode into disarray.

No… It wasn’t just Wilhelm’s carriage. All the vehicles carrying Zergev Squadron were likewise buffeted.

“So this is the stripping of the blessing to which Lady Mathers referred before we embarked.”

“It’s a forbidden technique for creating a blind spot in Odo Ragna… What a maddening entity…”

It was Pivot and Roswaal, respectively, who identified what had happened and why.

This was one of the traps Stride had laid in the Witch’s legacy they had brought from Shamrock Valley-the papers Roswaal had been decoding so intently.

For those who possessed a blessing, to lose that blessing was said to be akin to losing an arm or leg, or one’s eyes or ears-a sense or organ one had been born with. Many of the blessed could not cope with the experience, which they had never endured before. Sometimes, completely unable to parse the sense of dislocation, they might even go mad.

That was why Roswaal had instructed them to make sure there was no one in the unit now who possessed a blessing.

“I doooon’t think you quite believed me,” Roswaal said.

“It’s not the first time I’ve known you to spout nonsense. But I can tell what’s bullshit with you and what isn’t.”

It took Roswaal a second to reply. “Now thaaaat is a killing blow.” She laughed happily. Apparently, Wilhelm’s remark had plucked on her heartstrings. She slid herself along her bench, cozying up to him.

“Hey,” he grunted, suspicious of what she was about to do, but she winked her blue eye at him.

“As a show of gratitude, let me give you one bit of advice: What you need now is not self-recrimination. It’s rage.” Wilhelm was speechless.

“Find a rage as clear as a still pool and focus it on the thought of the enemy you must destroy, and your sword will again reach the heights it once knew. Sword Devil Wilhelm Trias-is that not your name?”

Roswaal spoke his birth name as if offering a profound clue-as though to summon the devil of the sword who had fought his way through the Demihuman War and finally laid low the Sword Saint.

After a second, Wilhelm grumbled, “Can’t you ever just come out and say something straight? No need to blather on when you could just tell me:No point in you thinking about it, idiot.”

“Call it the expression of a woman’s heart who wanted to spend every last moment she could speaking with you.”

It was profoundly relaxed banter, considering they were on the cusp of a battle. But they had traded such words during the war, too, and the thought brought Wilhelm back to when he had been the Sword Devil.

With that resolution in his heart, he turned without hesitation to look where the carriage was going, his blue eyes gazing into the distance.

An instant later, a shockwave came at them, blowing the carriages from their course.

“Mmmve it!” yelped Grimm, his shout coming even before the shockwave hit. To Wilhelm, it sounded inordinately loud.

Thanks to Grimm’s yell, he was in time to grab Roswaal with one arm. With his free hand, he drew his sword, thrusting it into the side of the carriage and plunging out the improvised exit.

At the same instant, the crimson shockwave truly showed its teeth, swallowing up the dragon carriage like a surging sea. As Wilhelm watched the carriage get swept away out of his peripheral vision, he realized he had escaped the same fate by a matter of seconds.

The others, however, were not so fortunate, and the highway was instantly turned into utter chaos.

Wilhelm landed on the ground and observed the awful scene. “Our unit! From tooth to tail…,” he growled, grinding his teeth.

He could see that more than half of Zergev Squadron had possessed the presence of mind to leap clear of their carriages and had jumped down, but the casualties among those who hadn’t were immense. Many of the carriages had been smashed beyond recognition. It was probably too much to hope anyone in them was still alive.

“I can’t believe this,” a voice groaned. It did indeed sound like the owner could barely believe what they were seeing-it was Roswaal, still clutched tight against Wilhelm’s side.

To see the normally unflappable woman so shocked brought home to him what a disaster this was, and he was about to shout orders to help the wounded when he realized: Roswaal wasn’t looking at the carriages. She was looking at the sky.

She stared upward, her multicolored eyes wide and an expression of pure shock on her face. And she wasn’t alone-everyone else who had avoided serious injury was staring, too.

And then…

“Wiiielm…”

Grimm, who had also safely escaped the disintegrating carriage, pointed at the sky and called Wilhelm’s name. Only at the urging of his friend with the huge shield on his back did Wilhelm finally look up.

Far in the distance, at the terminus of the highway, was their objective, the great city of Pictat. And high in the skies above it floated a vast, unsettling black cloud.

The black cloud beat its great wings and turned shimmering golden eyes upon the ground.

“No…”

Wilhelm rejected what he was seeing, tried to kill the weakness that made him attempt to force it into something he could understand.

That was no cloud. It was something anyone who lived in this world would recognize-but not something any of them should have had a chance to see with their own eyes. It was something that lived beyond the bounds of ordinary reason.

Namely…

“A dragon?”

The impossibly huge creature spread its black wings and hovered in the air over the merchant city. This was what had breathed destruction upon the soldiers racing to save the Dragonfriend Kingdom: a dragon. A dragon with three heads.

2

On the spire’s rooftop, the air was thick with the stomach-churning stench of blood. A river of crimson seeped out of a pile of corpses, each lying in a pool of gore, each cut down by a beautiful stroke of the sword. The life had drained out of them. Now they were simply inertthings. And the one who was forced to repeatedly take the lives of those chosen for sacrifice, much against her will, was…

“Carol!”

Carol Remendes, with her beloved sword in hand and dressed for battle.

Once, the sight of her in combat regalia had been frequent, but of late, there had been fewer and fewer appearances. This showed both how Carol was distancing herself from the battlefield, and how the kingdom was distancing itself from its time of war.

In time, Theresia had suspected, Carol’s valiant, battle-ready figure would be relegated to ceremonies and rituals. The possibility had made her at once sad and overjoyed.

Now that same woman was bathed in blood, with the sword she had so carefully honed defiled.

Carol was silent. Neither anger nor sadness resided any longer in her green eyes. She clutched her sword tightly, the tears that ran down her cheeks washed away by more sprays of blood. All that remained was a silent, unspeakable plea.

Not for forgiveness. But for punishment.

Carol, debased in both mind and body by the manipulation of the Ten Proud Commandments, wished to atone for her sins.

Theresia didn’t care who it was who had first planted the seed that gave rise to that desire for atonement. She only wished she could run up to Carol, embrace her, and gather up the pieces of her broken heart.

That, however, she could not do. Not because of the shackles on her feet or the curse on her unborn child. No, it was another “hope of victory” that Stride had prepared that prevented her. “My blessing…”

She could no longer feel it.

She had lost the her connected to two blessings, that of the Sword Saint and that of the reaper, and with this came a sense of loss greater than she had ever imagined. Indeed, she had never pictured such loss at all.

The blessing of the Sword Saint, passed down through generations of the Astrea family, was said to be the one blessing that could be received after birth. It could be inherited while the current possessor was still alive and well. Theresia herself had inherited the blessing from her uncle when he still lived. So she had been aware of and prepared for the possibility that one day, the blessing of the Sword Saint might be taken from her hands.

But this was different. She had lost not only the Sword Saint’s blessing, but the reaper’s as well-and that she had been born with. No… She hadn’t lost it. It had gone dormant.

She suspected, moreover, that she was not the only person to whom this had happened. This had to be the far edge of one of Stride’s plans as he turned his hatred upon something she could not see. Yes, only the far edge. She knew, for his scheme involved more than the stripping away of blessings.

“Truly, it is magnificent when seen from so close,” Stride said. There was a hint of genuine passion in his otherwise cold smile. Perhaps this, too, was something that had finally come to fruition. A shadow fell over him and all those who had joined him on the bloodstained rooftop. The powerful wind stirred up by the vast shape blew Theresia’s long red hair everywhere, but she couldn’t take her eyes off what was above them: a massive form with huge wings spread against the sky and scales as dark as steel. Its heads, three of them attached to one body, were a cross between a lizard’s and a snake’s, and they gazed at the scene below with golden eyes.

The menace of it, the monstrousness, belonged to the most powerful creature imaginable, which defied all normal laws: a three-headed black dragon. It drifted down through the sky above Pictat, beating its wings.

“Oh…”

Everyone born and raised in the Kingdom of Lugunica grew up learning that they were under the protection of the Holy Dragon. None of them had ever seen the creature, of course, but they naturally learned to regard dragons with profound respect.

Theresia was no different. She’d always had a subconscious gratitude and respect toward dragons. But to encounter one face-to-face was a new experience for the Sword Saint.

Worse, and almost impossible to believe, that dragon was under the control of the walking disaster.

“The Jade Pointer, the Amber Middle,andthe Sky-Blue Ring Finger,” Stride said. “Three heads and three souls demanded three of my fingers- greedy beast.”

He held his left hand toward the heavens, several of the fingers sparkling cruelly. As he had cursed Carol, and Tishua, and Theresia’s child, he now sought to bring the black dragon’s soul to heel with a spell.

The dragon, however, would not be constrained so easily.

All three of its heads roared mightily, and its tail lashed up a great wind as it fought against Stride’s control. It went beyond sound, as if the roar might slaughter the man so arrogant as to seek to manipulate a dragon.

The dragon’s tail strike, however, did not reach Stride. Kurgan intervened, catching the blow on his swords, while the dragon’s follow-up with its claws was intercepted by the two shinobi, changed into shadows, and Carol slashed at the wind stirred up by the flapping of its wings. Between them, they protected the man who stood at the center of this storm of hatred.

As Theresia took in the nightmarish scene, Melinda tugged on her sleeve. “This way.” She guided Theresia away from the whirlwind, holding up her arms to try to protect Theresia from flying debris and dust.

Theresia did not argue but stood behind Melinda. Mocking laughter reached her ears.

“Do you see this, Sword Saint? This dragon struggles pitifully and in vain, but it has lost its center; it is only a shell of a wyrm. Following its inborn instincts, it has descended to take back its true body, bathed in the blood of sacrifice.”

“The blood…of sacrifice?”

As the dragon continued to rain blows upon them, Stride’s pawns reacting to every attack, Stride himself struggled for supremacy with the black dragon’s very soul. Theresia, her eyes wide at his mocking words, gasped and looked around. She found the reason for his ridicule in the pile of corpses Carol had cut down.

She saw the skull of a nameless dragonfolk, three horns growing from its head.

Theresia was not aware of what it meant. Nor did she understand the connection between this dragon person, reduced to a skull, and the threeheaded black beast. All she knew was that these corpses were what the black dragon was here for, and that the shedding of blood had been a ritual to summon it.

And she realized one thing further: The eyes of one of the dragon’s heads had turned jade green.

“Countless demi-humans were all too eager to offer themselves up for sacrifice in the knowledge that it would ensure Lugunica’s destruction,” Stride said. “A rampaging dragon summoned by their blood… Could there be a more fitting way to shatter the duplicity of the Dragonfriend Kingdom?”

“Wait-” Theresia began, but her cry was too late. Stride’s glowing index finger was already pointed at the horizon-at the highway that ran out above Pictat as far as the eye could see. A breath of destruction was already being unleashed upon it.

In the far distance, a red light swept the earth, and she saw a cloud of smoke rise. Shortly after, the wind and noise of the blast reached the spot where she stood, a great distance away. The city itself seemed to shake beneath her feet, evidence of the dragon’s unparalleled destructiveness.

In spite of this demonstration, the fear she could not name went on-for there were still two more heads.

“I see it will not submit easily. But it is only a matter of time,” Stride said, winking.

Beside him, Kurgan lowered his sword and said in a quiet voice, “It is done trying to shake us off. Now we need only wait for the advent of a hero with the right to challenge us.”

Kurgan had been protecting Stride from the black dragon, but there was no need for that now. With one of its three heads under Stride’s control, the dragon’s thrashing gradually subsided. The two remaining heads, however, continued to fight not to be swallowed by the rings’ spells, frothing at the mouths.

As Stride said, it was probably just a matter of time until the dragon was under his control. And when it was, the unthinkable would happen: The creature would trample the Dragonfriend Kingdom underfoot.

Ignoring Theresia, whose every nerve was tense and ready for battle, one of the shinobi peered into the distance where the smoke was rising. “My lord, there appears to be movement beyond the impact of the breath.”

Stride, sparing some of his attention from his attempt to control the dragon, said, “Be exact. Was this movement forward or back?” “I believe it was an advance, sire,” said the other shinobi.

“Hee… Ha-ha! Ha-ha-ha-ha-ha-ha!” Stride laughed. It was laughter neither of mockery nor cold cruelty, but somehow without venom. It was the giggle of a naughty child who had succeeded in pulling a little prank. It sounded unbalanced and warped. When he had cackled his fill, Stride’s black eyes burned brightly, and he spat, “So the writer will not allow any deviations from fate, eh, my observers?!” Then he said, “Raizo! Shasuke! My generals ought to be upon the board. The opportunity you wished for has come at last. As I promised, I shall use you both up.”

“As you wish, sire!” they responded in unison, bowing deeply, and then the sank into the shadows.

When he was sure they were gone, Stride looked up at the hulking form of Kurgan beside him. His dark eyes met Kurgan’s red ones, and a moment of silence passed between them.

They did not, however, sink into the quiet. Instead, Stride said, “Go, Eight-Arms Kurgan. And do as you have wished for so long.”

“So I shall,” Kurgan replied. “And you, Stride, shall realize your grand ambition.”

It seemed wrong to interpret that as nothing more than an order and an answer. However, with that short exchange, the Empire’s most powerful war god sprinted across the roof and leaped down into the city, there to meet his enemy. A demonic aura radiated from him.

Once he had watched the great form vanish from the rooftop, Stride looked up at the black dragon, which continued to resist him. Without taking his eyes off the sky, he called to his wife. “Melinda, take the Sword Saint and go back into the tower. What of those enslaved by your eyes?”

“Oh… E-everything is already taken care of, my lord.”

“Good. Then do your duty as my wife. That is the purpose of your miserable little life.”

“Yes, my lord…!” Melinda nodded, putting her hands over her chest as if to still a racing heart. As a flush of red tinged her white cheeks, she once again took Theresia by the hand and made to guide her back into the spire.

Theresia, however, resisted the strength in her hand. “Stride!” she shouted at the walking disaster. He took note of her without even turning around, and she fretted over what she should say to him. “Carol… You’ve no more need of her, do you?”

“Do not speak a wish you know cannot come true. Such is nothing but the twittering of a helpless chick.” Theresia gasped.

“It is only the strong who are entitled to voice their desires. And you are not among them.”

Theresia’s lip began to quiver furiously at the way Stride saw straight through her thin ray of hope. He raised his hand as if to indicate he would hear no more appeals, and the burgundy glow took Theresia’s words from her.

The shinobi had gone, and Kurgan had left, and now even Melinda was being told to withdraw. As Stride maneuvered to control the black dragon on the roof, the only one left with him was Carol. Theresia could imagine how she must feel, and the thought squeezed hard at her heart. Before she was dragged back into the spire, she wanted to land at least one blow on him…

“Doyouhave it?” she asked. “Doyouhave the right to trample on the hopes of so many people?”

“…Go.”

Theresia had expected him to reply without hesitation that he did have the right, but instead, Stride coldly dodged the question. Almost as though, deep within his bones, he knew he had no such right.

3

The appearance of the black dragon, and the ravening of its breath, had thrown Wilhelm’s unit into absolute chaos.

Wilhelm looked on. A dragon, which had not been seen in decades, or perhaps even a hundred years and more, had appeared and savagely attacked the squadron. Now the three-headed black beast floated over the city. It was inconceivable this was not somehow connected to Stride and his faction.

Which meant he could even control dragons…

“No. The enemy doesn’t yet have complete control over the creature. That’s our chance,” said Roswaal, who amidst all the bellowing of orders, shouting for help for the wounded, and general chaos caused by the dragon’s appearance, had gotten her wits about her quicker than most. With her hand, she wiped at the blood running from her forehead.

“Are you insane?” asked Bordeaux.

“I daresay I am. My dear Bordeaux, alloooow me to give you a word of advice.”

He nodded at her forceful tone. “Please do.”

“That dragon there is undoubtedly Stride’s trump card. His spiriting away the Sword Saint using the Ten Proud Commandments, the stripping of the blessings via the burden that is the legacy of the Demi-human War, and now, of all things, an attempt to trample the Dragonfriend Kingdom under the feet of a dragon-each is a play for destruction.”

“Speaking as one of the people who has to fight him, I have to admit he knew exactly how to prepare for this.”

“Yes, I agree. Hoooowever, there is still a way to make inroads on him.

And as proof…”

“No…follow-up,” rasped Grimm, catching on to Roswaal’s implication as he watched the dragon in the distance.

Roswaal snapped her fingers and nodded. “Precisely. He’s already bloodied our noses. If each of that dragon’s heads were to spew its breath, we could never get close to the city-which reveals that our opponent has not yet gained full control of the creature. We do not, however, have time to dawdle. In other words…”

“Right now, we’re the only ones who can make it in time,” Wilhelm concluded, the fruit of his warrior’s intuition.

Bordeaux, silent, crossed his beefy arms and wavered between advance and retreat. Not that Wilhelm was planning to flee even if that was what Bordeaux chose to do.

At that moment, a great voice rippling with vigor and anger cried, “Mad Dog Bordeaux!”

It was not Roswaal, nor Wilhelm, nor Grimm either. The shout had come from Conwood, who had been listening to the discussion. In his eyes could be seen his profound sense of duty-eyes he now turned upon Bordeaux. And he was not the only one.

All the knights there who could still do battle-no, even those who were so badly wounded that they could no longer be expected to serve in combat- had but one thought in mind.

“Let’s fight,” Conwood said. “To protect the kingdom. And the Sword Saint…and the honor of our own blades.”

At that, everyone present thrust their swords into the air, demonstrating how knights of the kingdom should behave.

Bordeaux closed his eyes. In the scales of his heart, he was weighing his duty against his desire to fight, and one side proved heavier.

“What a lot of goddamned fools you are,” he grumbled, his one concession to his old, vulgar manner of speaking, and then he hefted his halberd onto his shoulder. He turned slowly to look up at the dragon that gazed down upon the earth from the distant sky.

It did not take him long to arrive at his decision.

4

“Looks like we won our bet,” Wilhelm muttered once his “do-or-die unit” had successfully infiltrated the city.

There had been a suggestion that they should split the group into four and approach Pictat from each direction, just in case anything or anyone got in their way, but in the end, they decided the unit should make a single, concentrated strike.

They adopted a formation that prioritized speed and offensive power, but as they had somewhat suspected, there were no obstacles on the road, and no further breath attacks came from the dragon. Now that they were this close to it, they could tell it wasn’t just saving its attacks.

The creature was unimaginably large, dozens of meters long, and covered in scales that glittered dark like steel. With its three terrifying heads that could project impossibly powerful breath, it was indeed the very beast that had been feared from time immemorial.

At this moment, however, the black dragon was twisting in the air, all three heads howling furiously.

It was clear the creature was no longer free and that it was struggling against undesired control. Roswaal had been right: This was their best chance to get at Stride.

“But that opportunity is going to slip away from us the longer we wait. This is a race against time,” Roswaal said.

“Unfortunately, we’ve got our hands full with Stride and his people. I don’t have the luxury of getting into a fight with time itself, too. Not to mention, after we take care of all of that, we might still have to slay a black dragon,” Wilhelm said.

Even if the three-headed creature slipped from Stride’s control, it wasn’t clear whether the dragon would be friendly toward them. It was entirely possible that after dealing with Stride’s forces, they would still have a battle with the dragon on their hands.

“Ah, there’s my threatening fighter.Howpleasant to be able to laugh and say that’s what makes you, you.” Roswaal, running beside Wilhelm, chuckled at his total lack of fear of the monster.

All the while this conversation was going on, the squadron raced down the city’s main avenue, toward the central district-toward the spire above which the black dragon hovered. They didn’t know exactly where Stride and the others were, but if he was fighting to control the dragon, then it stood to reason he would be squarely beneath it.

“Wait! Look at that!” one of the knights cried, and Wilhelm and the others in front skidded to a halt.

From ahead of the squadron, human figures began shambling into the street. For a second, the soldiers thought they might be assassins sent by Stride, but they soon saw this was not the case. The weapons the figures carried and the armor they wore was worked with designs showing they belonged to the city.

“I think that’s Pictat’s garrison,” one of the knights said, and agreement quickly spread. Wilhelm, glad to see allies from whom he could learn about the situation on the ground, began to let his vigilance lapse.

Grimm, however, took a step forward, his expression hard. He didn’t make a sound, but other than Theresia, there was nothing in this world that Wilhelm trusted as much as Grimm’s sense of caution.

Grimm turned out to be right.

“Hey… This doesn’t make any sense…”

As one knight noticed the aberration, his voice began to tremble, and he looked all around. The sound of countless footsteps began to pound down the streets, filling avenues wide enough for several dragon carriages to pass by each other comfortably.

First there was just one person, then five, then ten, and suddenly it was a dark mass of figures. They walked at a trot, pushing and jostling, shoving their way forward.

By the time Wilhelm registered they were in trouble, they were already trapped. “Get your shields up, everyone!” Bordeaux bellowed. “We’ll pick a single point and drive through! They’re going to crush us!”

“Hrrraaaah!” the knights cried instantly, and then with Grimm, who moved faster than anyone, at their head, they raised their huge shields and met the wave of people head-on-only to hear a massive crash.

Shouts of distress accompanied the terrible impact, and their ears were assaulted by the sounds of rending flesh and shattering bones. The sound came again and again as the wall of flesh and blood tried to stop the unit from moving forward.

Bordeaux, with his halberd outthrust and attempting to fight the human wave, ground his teeth. “Why?! Don’t tell me the city guard has gone over to

Stride’s side!”

“No! Look at their eyes!” Wilhelm shouted.

“What?!”

Wilhelm, who was battering people back with his sword still sheathed, pointed to his own eyes. “There’s something wrong with their eyes! I’ve seen this before-in Stride’s companions!”

“That girl whose gaze you met through the mirror… Her eyes had the same pattern in them.”

Pivot looked around as Wilhelm shouted, and his words brought back a memory. The day he had failed to kill Stride in the Astrea manor, there had been a woman. Their eyes had met through the conversation mirror. It was her -she was the one who had caused him to see the phantom Pivot.

Now, all the city guards who stood against Wilhelm and his friends had the same spiderweb pattern in their eyes, just like the woman; it had ensnared their hearts.

“The Evil Eye Clan? Fiiiirst Kurgan, then shinobi, now this? Stride keeps changing his little tricks. He seems to have everything ready,” Roswaal sighed, her guess triggered by Wilhelm’s words. She dodged the guards’ attacks with quick, deft movements and responded with hammer blows of her fist that deprived them of consciousness.

Bordeaux, Conwood, and the rest were not quite as flamboyant as Roswaal, but they used their skill, far greater than any of the city guards’, to parry, strike back, and somehow avoid being crushed.

Eventually, however, numbers would tell. They might be able to keep up this struggle for a few more minutes if they were lucky.

“We have to tip the balance in our favor, somehow,” Roswaal said. “We have to be ready to cut them down.”

There in the midst of the battle, Wilhelm met her multicolored eyes and ground his teeth.

As ever, Roswaal was willing to play the villain, willing to say the things someone had to say-and her words lit a fire under Wilhelm, who had so far hesitated to draw his sword.

He cursed the cruel plot that had pitted him against the Pictat city guard, fellow subjects of the King-and then, he prepared to make his terrible choice.

“Iiihelm!”

If he hadn’t reacted instantaneously to Grimm’s voice, whipping his sword out of its scabbard, he would have died.

With a gasp, he drew his sword up to one side, deflecting the steel blade that came at him with the speed of a bullet.

The force of the blow shook his entire body, and for a moment, he lost his footing and stumbled backward. But he wasn’t the only one hopping over the pavement-so was the opponent who had jumped at him.

The enemy charged with a cry, so fast he hardly seemed to touch the ground. He came on like a tumbling boulder, manifested in eight arms, four of which held Devil Cleavers. A true war god, perhaps the ultimate.

“Well met, Sword Devil. I’m impressed you survived the black dragon’s breath.”

“Me, I would’ve been just as happy never to see your face again, EightArms Kurgan.”

Kurgan had landed in a crouch, so forcefully that the pavement cracked beneath him. Wilhelm met his awful grin with a glare of his own, dripping with rage that welled up from deep within him.

Kurgan had descended into the battle on the avenue from an impossible angle. Quite honestly, without Grimm’s warning, Wilhelm’s life would have been over, and the battle would already be decided.

“Wilhelm, we’ve gotten separated from the young man and his people,”

Pivot said into his ear. “At this rate-”

Wilhelm nodded. “Yeah, I know! Roswaal! Can you-”

He looked around the battlefield. Kurgan’s headlong charge had opened a vast space in the scrum, amid which Wilhelm could barely discern ally from enemy. But Grimm and the others might be able to use it as an opportunity to break through the guards and go after Stride.

He saw-he accepted-that his role now was to fight Kurgan to the death.

But…

“She’s gone?” he mumbled, his eyes wide.

Roswaal, who should have been somewhere on the battlefield with its freshly opened breathing space, was nowhere to be seen. Wilhelm felt a twinge of panic. Surely, she hadn’t been caught up in Kurgan’s charge and blown aside, had she? But panic soon changed to sheer amazement, for Wilhelm’s attention was caught by something else. The shadows around the battle began to ripple like water.

It was the same way the shadows had shimmered when he had missed his chance to kill Stride-the sign of the shinobi moving among them. They’d slipped in amid the chaos and had taken Roswaal away.

For a second, his mind went blank with white heat, but a bellow from Bordeaux brought him back. “Don’t get distracted, Wilhelm! Grimm went with her!”

Wilhelm blinked, then took courage from the sight of the giant man swinging his polearm, sending guards flying left and right. He was right. Wilhelm didn’t see Grimm, either.

There was no telling what might await them on this battlefield, but he would leave Grimm and Roswaal to their own fights.

And he had to, for Wilhelm had no room to stand still as he confronted this most potent of enemies.

“I give thanks for a worthy foe,” Kurgan said. “This is the end for

Lugunica. A fitting arena for our final battle.”

“You still like to prattle, huh? I’m not gonna spend long on you.”

“If it be so, then let us make these few exchanges the greatest of our lives.”

With that, the Sword Devil and Eight-Arms set upon each other at a charge.

A second Silver Flower Dance bloomed in the very center of the chaos of Pictat.

5

When he was released from the shadows, Grimm found himself robbed of his sense of balance, hardly able to tell up from down. He reached out for the ground, somehow able to limit himself to simply falling to one knee. No sooner had he done so than he took a great leap backward, raising the huge shield bearing the Remendes crest, ready for an attack.

None came, however. For that matter, this place he had crossed the shadows to reach…

“I give you one little chore, and you still can’t do it. Truly, my generals leave much to be desired. To what end have you brought me this uninvited guest, this…ordinaryman? Go ahead. Give me your excuse.”

“It appears that he possesses fearsome intuition, sire. He clung to the arm of the woman you wanted.”

“Fool. If you didn’t have the wherewithal to account for that, what is it but a mark of your own failure?”

Grimm watched the exchange, every muscle in his body taut and ready. One of the speakers was a thin man with long, purple hair, while the other was a shinobi in a black outfit who responded with utmost respect. Grimm could guess who they were from the conversation, but even if he couldn’t have, this was someone who was burned into his memory so thoroughly that he might as well have been carrying around a name card.

This man was the one who had brought the nation of Lugunica to the brink of destruction: the walking disaster, Stride.

“Well, well, weeeell. I certainly didn’t expect to receive a personal summons from the root of all evil,” said the beautiful woman standing beside Grimm. As breezy as she sounded, she looked ready for combat, and she didn’t appear injured. That was a relief. She was Grimm’s comrade-in-arms, Roswaal, and a friend Carol cherished.

He was glad that the instant those shadows had shifted, he had jumped in without a thought.

“Thank you kindly, Grimm,” Roswaal said. “Because of you, I don’t have to witness this all on my own.”

“Yehh,” he answered. He nodded at Roswaal, the wind prickling his skin as it blew over them. In this, too, he and she were in accord. Neither of them should be there alone.

Not on this battlefield, where directly overhead, the three-headed black dragon continued to fight Stride’s spell. Its howls shook the air, and it cried out as if it would annihilate the whole world.

Grimm and Roswaal had been ejected from the shadows onto the spire rooftop, where the dragon was stirring up a tremendous gale. It had certainly saved them covering the distance from the battle on the thoroughfare to the spire, and now they found themselves directly confronting the enemy leader.

Leering at their amazement, Stride spread his hands. “Something to see, is it not? A dragon, alleged to be the greatest creature in existence, beyond mortal imagining-yet it’s unable to shake off the spells of a half-dead man like me. Look at it fight!”

“Maybe I’m noooot one to talk, but I don’t think this is a very respectable hobby,” Roswaal said.

“Hoh, you disapprove of my pastimes, do you? I thought you of all people might appreciate fine entertainment, but I seem to have misjudged you.”

“For my reference, may I ask what made you think that?”

“There’s no cute logic to it. It’s because you came closer to my plans than any other, O mage of the kingdom.” Stride’s smile widened, and he gazed at Roswaal with eyes full of evil. He didn’t even register Grimm’s presence. He was focused entirely on Roswaal, who had uncovered so much of his plot.

Well, good-Grimm could use that as an opportunity to find a gap in Stride’s defenses.

“I humbly recommend against rashly turning a hand upon him,” said one of the shinobi, ever vigilant for their master’s safety. So much for any impetuous bids for victory. He glanced over. It looked like Roswaal was trying to draw as much information out of Stride as she could. Grimm, playing along with her plan, tried to stay calm.

The black dragon was terrible, but if this was the heart of the enemy’s stronghold, then what they wanted was here-the kidnapped Theresia and the enslaved Carol.

“So you’re saying because I had you more cornered than anyone, I get the prize for fighting spirit? I can’t tell you how grateful I am. I’ve been eeeever so eager to split your head open.”

“I wouldn’t imagine those to be the words of one of the kingdom’s best and brightest, and a woman so versed in magic. But very well. I will not be so condescending as to call it an award for fighting spirit. No, this is a plot for you.”

“For…me?” Roswaal narrowed her eyes. She didn’t like the sound of that.

Just then, there was a soft thump of feet landing on the rooftop, but the noise of the wind stirred up by the dragon blocked it out. A sword stroke flashed through the gale, aiming right at Roswaal’s neck.

Roswaal was about to meet it with the black leather gloves she wore-but Grimm caught the blow on his shield, saving her from the ambush. “Ahh won’t le’ you do thhha!” he cried.

No…he hadn’t saved her, exactly. Roswaal had seen the ambush coming. She would have protected herself even without Grimm’s intervention.

When Grimm leapt to cover the attack, it was not for Roswaal’s sake. It was for his own.

For the blade that had come at Roswaal from behind was wielded by…

“G…Grrr…Grimm!”

He heard it. From her trembling lips came his name-the name of the one who had blocked her very sword.

Covered in the blood of lives she had been forced to take stood the woman

Grimm loved. Carol Remendes was wielding her sword at the behest of

Stride’s spell.

When Grimm saw the streaks on her cheeks where her tears had dried, he instinctively reached out. He would have embraced her if he could have. With a deft twirl of her sword, she slipped away from his fingers and jumped back.

He saw fresh tears gleam in her eyes as she retreated.

“I knew this woman was a servant of the Sword Saint and a friend of yours, Mathers. Thus, she struck me as the perfect pawn to pit against you.

But no, now I see she is not.”

Carol, still weeping, stood at Stride’s side, taking up a fighting stance with perfect, measured movements. Stride took her chin in his hand without even turning toward her, his black eyes glinting.

Only then did he finally seem to remember Grimm was there.

“So…you’re the man who serves as her lover. Hah! Fate does bring us strange meetings. The Sword Saint and Mathers, and the man who loves this woman-I never expected you all to be here to amuse me!”

“No… No, no, no, no, no!”

“Still you have the spirit to resist? Your tears have not yet dried up? I tell you, it is most unusual to find a woman for whom weeping is so becoming. And you, sniveling rat-as a man, will you be enraged? For if not…”

Stride’s words, which had gone beyond simple cruelty to make one doubt his very humanity, were interrupted by a distinct crack.

“My lord, there is a limit to these jokes.”

“Hrmph.”

Stride dismissed the loyal shinobi’s advice with a sniff, but the shinobi did not appear particularly bothered by this. No matter how much his master abused him or poured out contempt on him, the shinobi would protect him- including from the piece of rooftop that Roswaal had broken off with her foot and launched at him as projectiles.

Her expression, calm and cold, radiated menace and dispassionate hostility. Grimm remembered seeing that look on her face once before, when she had faced the Witch.

Which was to say, now, Roswaal J Mathers was truly angry.

“Truth be told, I should make you spit out every last detail of your little plans,” she said. “But I tell you now: Shut your mouth, you little yapping dog. I can’t be bothered to listen to your voice anymore.”

“Hah! Now, there is an expression worth savoring. I like your eyes no more than you like mine. You might even say I harbor hatred for that blue eye of yours. Do you believe that if you set yourself a boundary, you can still avoid stepping off the path of common humanity? Foolish hauteur.” Roswaal didn’t speak.

“You and I are of a kind. Whether or not we wish it so.”

Roswaal and Stride faced each other, the hostility and enmity and hatred plain between them. Grimm watched them out of the corner of his eye as he kept his shield raised against Carol. Even now, she was so beautiful he could hardly take his eyes off her. All the blood, all the sword fighting, could not defile her when she showed the resolve to protect someone.

“Grimm… I’m sorry. I’m sorry! Please, you must-”

“Caaool, I lo…”

When Carol spoke, her voice strained and shot through with agony, he understood immediately what she was asking for. That was why he wouldn’t let her finish. He interrupted her and then, his cheeks taut, Grimm faced forward.

He knew what one should express to one’s beloved when she was crying. He had seen his dear friend the Sword Devil do it for the Sword Saint in front of a great crowd of the kingdom’s subjects.

And so he said, “I l’vvve…you.”

And then he braced his shield and caught the sword stroke delivered by the woman he loved, tears still streaming down her face.

The blows traded by Grimm Fauzen and Carol Remendes sent up sparks like a love song into the sky.

6

A great, vast battle had begun, with the kingdom’s existence hanging in the balance. Theresia could tell from the shivering in the air, from the shaking of the ground, and she heaved a long sigh.

Now, Theresia-with her blessings stripped from her and her child held hostage by a curse-found herself just an ordinary woman, a weakling with no way to fight or resist.

Everything seemed to be in Stride’s clutches, going exactly according to his plans.

Perhaps she should play the part of the helpless maiden and wait quietly for someone to rescue her.

But…

“Melinda, you’re controlling the members of the city guard with your Evil Eyes, aren’t you?” Theresia asked, not hesitating to broach the subject openly. Melinda made a sort of squeak.

There was not much Theresia could do. Brought back to the topmost floor of the spire and without even the freedom to open the window, she couldn’t so much as see what was going on outside.

The ritual to control the black dragon Stride had summoned was still going on above them. Carol was with him, but her heart must have been in tatters from being forced to serve him.

Which was exactly why Theresia couldn’t simply sit by and play the part of the captured princess.

“I beg you not to think of trying anything,” Melinda said. “My lord told me not to let you.”

“Are you also being controlled by one of his rings?”

“M…me? Under a ring’s spell?” Melinda asked, stumbling over the words.

“That’s a no? Of course not. I’m sorry. That was very mean of me to ask.”

Theresia did feel genuinely bad for the woman, but she needed to bring her into the arena of conversation, so she ignored Melinda’s confusion and drew her into a battle of wits and words. By bringing up a subject Melinda couldn’t ignore-by inquiring whether she was aiding Stride of her own free will-the woman wouldn’t be able to help saying something in response.

And indeed, she did. Theresia pressed the advantage.

“So you’re helping Stride of your own free will. Your reasons… Well, I can imagine there are a few. My husband and I are just the same, so I understand. But how does Stridereallyfeel?”

“What are you…trying to say?”

“You may care for him, but that doesn’t guarantee it goes both ways. Don’t you think he may simply be using you? That he may just want the power of the Evil Eye Clan?”

These words were so cruel that it took courage to speak them.

The Evil Eye Clan to which Melinda, with her eyes shut, belonged were a group of demi-humans so rare that some said they didn’t exist anymore. Somewhere in their body was a “Evil Eye” that possessed a kind of power different from magic, spells, or blessings. Sometimes, these eyes could see invisible things or even interfere with other people’s minds.

The reason there were so few Evil Eye Clan members left was because the Empire, fearing that unique power, had exterminated them.

As it happened, it was not so different from how the kingdom had treated its half-elves. Melinda herself had probably experienced severe oppression and had maybe been in danger of her life.

Then perhaps her feelings were in part for the one who had saved her from that oppression…

“We’ve seen for a fact that Stride is using your Evil Eye as he pleases. So

-”

“Yes, he’s using me. What’s the matter with that?” Theresia’s breath caught.

“All that great man seeks from me is the reprehensible power of my Evil Eye. Yes, yes, oh yes! That is good. It is my bliss that such a great man seeks anything from me.”

Theresia was ashamed of herself when she heard this answer. This was neither admiration nor infatuation. She supposed it was impossible Stride truly loved Melinda as his wife. But Melinda, understanding that perfectly well, nonetheless loved Stride as her husband. Theresia was intensely embarrassed she had tried to change that wordloveto something else and use it for her own ends.

“His greatness was cast aside by his native land. He shines with the light of one who, though beaten down, clings on, cursing fate. He is the guide of those who have been cast aside by history and fate. That great man is the

poison who will kill the observers who sit in heaven.” Theresia could not speak.

“To that end, I am his cornerstone. To that end, I use my accursed Eyes. I was born with Evil Eyes in both sockets, an accursed child who destroyed the town of her own birth. For this, I was brought into the world.”

Melinda was driven by this burden, by a grim resolve, by an unshakable conviction-no, no. She was motivated by love. She truly believed that for the man she loved, it would not be too much even to lay down her life.

Theresia knew she had to meet that true belief by showing that she, too, possessed that resolve.

“P…please, don’t try anything funny,” Melinda said. Even though her eyes were closed, she seemed acutely aware of what Theresia was doing. Theresia didn’t know if it was a sound she made, or something Melinda sensed on her skin, but the fact was that she issued this warning the moment Theresia stood up.

Of course, shackled and without her blessings, there was little Theresia could do-but she might be able to convince Melinda, who knew nothing of battle, that she could fight.

“The child… Don’t forget the spell on your child. The price of your actions will be its life.”

“That’s true, and it frightens me. Truly it does. But I am the Sword Saint. At this moment, when the kingdom itself may be in danger, I simply can’t stand quietly by!”

“Y-you would risk your child’s life just for that title? For a misplaced sense of duty?”

“Whether I wish it or not, Wilhelm’s and my child will face trials in its life. That is what it means to be an Astrea, after all. This child can no more escape its destiny than I can-as much as I wish it could live a peaceful, quiet life as just another human being, blessed with happiness.”

Theresia’s hands brushed her swollen belly. This wish for her baby’s future peace was the one true thing she said.

Yet, at the same time, she knew a life free of disruption was not in store for her child. She couldn’t clear away every pebble on the road that it would walk. And thus…

“As this child belongs to the Astreas, it, too, must fight. For me, and my husband, and this kingdom. That is the destiny of the line of the Sword Saints.” Theresia’s blue eyes met Melinda’s closed ones.

At Theresia’s declaration, Melinda began to quiver-first her hands, then her shoulders, then her lips. “Wh…wh…what hubris. You w-w-would not protect the child as it deserves, but make it fight? I’ve h-h-had enough of you. I don’t believe I can f-forgive you.”

With that, Theresia sensed a great wave of hostility overflowing from beyond the veil of confusion. Melinda’s expression was hard, and slowly, she opened her eyes-her Evil Eyes.

“My right eye is the Evil Eye of Arrogance. My left is the Evil Eye of Ostentation.”

“Oh…”

The moment Theresia saw the beautiful, mind-bending spiderweb pattern in Melinda’s eyes, she lost her footing. She felt as if her soul were being swallowed, falling, falling, ever falling.

“You’re going to a deep, dark sea bottom of guilt and regret. The child in your belly has done nothing wrong. Only you, its mother the Sword Saint, have committed a sin that cannot be forgiven. I tell you to remember it.”

The voice Theresia was hearing, Melinda’s rancor, grew farther and farther away. She heard it at the far edges of her consciousness as her soul slipped into the abyss.

“Wilhelm…”

She called the name of her dear husband, just once. And then, Theresia was overcome by darkness.

CHAPTER 6: ACT VI

Flash of Splendor

1

Theresia drifted in void. She felt like she was sinking into a deep, dark abyss.

In this place, even her own hands and feet barely seemed present. She touched her belly and apologized. In her womb, there was an infant waiting for its moment to be born. This crystallization of the love between Theresia and Wilhelm, the Sword Saint and the Sword Devil, was facing a threat that touched its very life before it even came into the world.

If Theresia could not rise back up out of the darkness, the child would never have a chance to be born…

“I will never, ever let that happen,” Theresia said, and her voice was that of a mother, quiet but intensely determined. Whatever might await her, shewouldsee this child safely through.

The sea bottom met Theresia, resolve and all, and the deep darkness split open to reveal…

“Yes…of course. If this is supposed to show me the sins I’ve committed, then there’s only one thing I could see,” she said, looking out over crimsonstained land where she now stood.

The wind was dry, the sky so high and far away that it seemed to have forsaken the earth itself. Theresia stood on top of a tower, built of ill-fitting stones and already half destroyed.

As far as she could see in every direction were figures, staring up at her with empty eyes. They reached out with bloodstained fingers, raised aggrieved howls like the groaning of the earth. It was a horde of the dead.

She recognized each and every one of these corpses-they were all people Theresia had killed.

The Sword Saint had taken up her sword to fight the Demi-human War, and in its name, she had taken countless lives.

If it was true there was neither noble nor base in life, but all lives weighed equal, then these scales were wildly unbalanced. If, then, these dead wished to denounce her, Theresia had no right to deny them.

“Is this…where my sins have brought me?”

She looked out on the crowd of the dead, the evidence of her transgression, and her knees shook. Instinctively, her body sought to curl up on the ground, but she covered her belly with her hands and thought of the life within.

As those to whom she had dealt death jostled and shoved to be the first to reach her, a precious life remained inside her, one that she had committed herself to welcoming into this world. And so she stood tall, facing the horde.

“Please,” she said. “Give me courage, Wilhelm.”

They were not the words of the Sword Saint, for Theresia was not the Sword Saint, but simply a woman. She offered the prayer from deep in her heart-before, dodging past the fingers of the dead, she leaped from the crumbling tower of her own volition.

In this world in thrall to the Evil Eye of Arrogance, she faced a battle with her own sins.

2

A terrible struggle was likewise brewing outside, set against the backdrop of the merchant city of Pictat.

In the heavens was a black dragon, on the earth were people, all blessings had been taken from the world, and the child of disaster only chuckled.

Standing on the roof of the tower that overlooked the city, Stride, the Death Wish, spread his hands wide and listened to the dragon’s howling echo through the city with total satisfaction.

“The stage is now set, and the actors assembled,” he said. “The Sword Saint is reduced to an ordinary person, blessings have been stripped away, and the salvation of the Dragon will not come. The time of the end is near, O cruel observers! What will the next move be, eh?!”

His eyes gleamed brightly, and though his face was that of a man half dead, his voice brimmed with vigor. His shout was not aimed at anyone in particular but was a wild, mocking cry at the entire world. Anyone who had seen him would have marveled at the power that hatred could give a man.

Behind Stride, whose black outfit whipped in the wind stirred up by the dragon, was another battlefield brought to Pictat by malice. It was a blend of the shinobis’ skills of sliding through the shadows and a woman whose physical prowess was backed up by bloody training.

Mathers, who had been hot on the trail of Stride’s plans through sheer ingenuity, likewise fought on this battlefield in a way Stride and his people had not expected. Why would a specialist in magic ever have bothered to master the martial arts?

Roswaal’s techniques, flowing one into the other, showed much to recommend themselves in this straightforward fight to the death. But what really held Stride’s interest was another, muddier battle.

“Hrrgh… Ahh!”

Tears still streaming from her already puffy eyes, Carol bellowed, her sword dancing.

It was unbecoming for a woman to present herself in battle, yet this one almost made up for that with the captivating beauty of her sword work. Each time the blade met the great shield, there was a sound almost like music, and sparks scattered across the rooftop.

The ringing of the great sword and the great shield against one another was not the sound of hatred or hostility; it was that of acri de coeurthat could not be brushed aside and a love that could not be pushed away. It was a clash unwished for, between two people in love.

“I cast my spell on her not merely for her strength, but because the relationships she bore fitted my purpose-and she proved an excellent fighter to boot. More than I expected from a servant.”

Stride watched the back-and-forth between the woman swordsman he’d constrained with his spell and the shield bearer who met each of her blows head-on. Stride himself, of course, was worth nothing in the heat of battle, but he had a good eye for excellent fighters. The battle before him now vindicated his judgment. But the longer it went on, the more it marred his drama.

“Hrk? Ah-Ahh! N-no, no! Grimm, ruuun!”

The weeping woman’s eyes glowed a faint burgundy. Then she started moving faster, such that even an untrained observer could tell. Her blows got harder, and the shield bearer, unable to stand his ground, was shoved backward.

“I have used my spell to force open the gate that was closed and flood her body with energy. This spell has been long forbidden, for it pushes the physical body past its limits-but if one of my puppets should break, what harm is that to me?”

“Ah… Ahh! Ahhhhh!”

The woman’s screams drowned out Stride’s cold murmur. Her fury might have been directed at him, but her brilliantly honed techniques were wielded against the man she claimed to love.

A power greater than her own innate ability was forced out of Carol, her bones creaking, her skin beginning to split. Even then, the storm of attacks did not abate. The shield bearer could not defend quickly enough, and it was only a matter of time before he would be swimming in a sea of blood.

The shield bearer, forced entirely onto the defensive, however, had a chance to turn the tide of battle. No fight could be won simply by letting oneself be hit again and again. So instead of defending, he had to pull off a reversal.

“Grimm… Please, you have to…”

…kill me.Presumably that was where the woman’s weeping entreaty was going.

Quite frankly, Stride had no intention of the women’s relentless sword dance ending any other way. A battle between two fools in love could only end with the man or the woman dying. One of them would perish.

If the man didn’t have it in him to do the deed, then so long as the woman could still be used against Mathers, this would only end when her sword split the skull of her beloved-or so Stride assumed. But his assumption was undercut the very next moment.

“What?”

The shield slipped from the man’s hands-no, he dropped it, presenting himself defenseless against the women’s next stroke.

“Cyyaroo,” he said, and as he spoke the woman’s name, his expression was horrendously…gentle.

The woman’s eyes went wide, and for an instance her arm bent, ready to cleave the man from head to loin.

The sound of steel rending bone and flesh, tearing it apart…did not come. The blow stopped an inch from the man’s forehead. A once-in-a-lifetime miracle of love? Certainly not.

“Yoou… Yoou know hhoww long ah’ve wathed yoou and th’ Sword Devil, Cyyaool,” said the man, who had shot his hands in the air and caught the blade between them.

One could not do that with a shield. One could defend with a shield, but only parry, deflect, pass aside. So the man had let go of the shield and put his life on the line to stop the woman from swinging the blade she did not wish to wield.

It had been unnecessary to risk his life for victory or even for logical reasons. This was the utter foolishness of love.

Pierced by the light in the man’s eyes, for the first time, Stride truly saw his opponent-the man they had called Grimm-and saw a value beyond that of a lover fighting with the puppet controlled by a spell.

His face twisted of its own accord-not from anger, but from pleasure.

Pleasure at the unexpected encounter with a miracle.

“You, of all people…?” Stride breathed.

“Whath yoou mean?”

“I mean…you! Could you possibly be the observers’ response, their true next move? Not the Sword Devil, but you?”

Grimm’s expression never went beyond one of incomprehension. But Stride did not even pause at the annoyance of this response. He had already made up his mind.

This called for a test. He had to find out if this man was the last wall he must scale in his life.

“Shasuke!”

Stride held up his right hand and the middle finger glowed, effulgent with an amber light, and the long hand of death reached through the shadows.

The great shadow cast by the black dragon rippled like the surface of a pond, and an instant later, the shinobi Stride had called for appeared behind the swordswoman. His blade glinted silver as it sought to take two lives at once.

The shinobi could use the woman as a wall and strike from safety, piercing Grimm’s heart in a single movement. Grimm had dropped his shield, and his hands were occupied with the woman’s sword, leaving him no way to defend himself. He couldn’t even see the shinobi.

The merciless attack would stop both lovers’ hearts at once.

“Not onmywatch.”

That she was able to catch up with a shinobi who could move across shadows in an instant was down to long, hard training in the art of motion. The distance between them simply vanished, and someone inserted themselves between the would-be killer and the swordswoman.

The blow sent shockingly bright-red blood splattering across the rooftop.

“Wha?” The swordswoman gasped when someone stumbled against her back. Finally becoming aware of the life-and-death struggle happening directly behind her, she turned her head as far as she could, moved her eyes as far as she was able-and then, she saw it.

Roswaal J Mathers had thrown herself in front of the oncoming thrust and allowed herself to be impaled.

Carol’s green eyes went wide at the sight, and she bellowed, “Julia!” Her terrible scream rent the air, echoing all around.

3

This conversation happened not long after Wilhelm started seeing the ghost of Pivot.

“When you come right down to it, I’m simply the sense of guilt that lingers in your heart.”

“Fine. I’ll listen to you.”

“Excellent. Then with gratitude, I shall continue. Although what I have to say is essentially nothing but your own thoughts.”Wilhelm didn’t respond.

“Wilhelm, you shouldn’t cling to this aberration forever.”

“Hold on. Me? Cling to you?”

“Yes, that’s right. I think you already realize I am not the real Pivot Anansi, former vice-captain of Zergev Squadron. I’m only a shadow, born of yourideaof Pivot-merely a manifestation of your own confusion.”

“That’s-”

“Not true? If it isn’t, then try asking me a deeply personal question. Something about Pivot Anansi’s hobbies or personal history, maybe his

family. I assure you, I can answer none of them.”Once again, Wilhelm said nothing.

“And the reason is, you didn’t know anything about Pivot. The illusion before you is ultimately only the vestige of the guilt that clings in a corner of your heart. I cannot know what you do not.”Still, Wilhelm was silent.

“The impetus and cause of this aberration, we can be certain of. The only riddle that truly remains is: Why me? But even there, I think you have an inkling. You, who were once only a sword, have begun to awaken to your humanity, and so you have become acquainted with guilt. And I am the first person whose death you ever regretted.”

“The first…death…”

“I am like a flickering flame and will gutter and disappear one day. The comrade whose death you mourn, Pivot Anansi, is already gone. You will have no chance to speak with him again.”Wilhelm was silent.

“Therefore, Wilhelm, there is something you must acknowledge.”Once again Wilhelm said nothing.

“Next, it will be your turn.”

“Is your mind not in this place?”

“Hngh!”

A heavy blow was the price Wilhelm paid for his waking dream and his lapse of attention. A cleaver came whistling at him-certain death. To avoid it, Wilhelm had to bet everything on his mastery of the blade and the strength of his sword; he met the blow with a rising strike that was powerful enough to smash the earth asunder.

There came a thunderous crash, followed by a tremendous impact. The air, without exaggeration, split, and the ground heaved upward. This was the destruction wrought by sword meeting sword, warrior and warrior, skill against skill. The battle between the Sword Devil and Eight-Arms brought devastation upon the city akin to a natural disaster.

“You have no time to be thinking of other things. Your sword is here, and mine is there. This is the most splendid stage of our lives; I would ask you not to waste it.”

“Your theatrical bullshit is the perfect match for your head-ass master! Yah!” Meeting Kurgan’s remark with a burst of bad attitude, Wilhelm spat out the blood that had pooled in his mouth.

Not a single attack had actually landed, but his opponent was Eight-Arms Kurgan, a god of war who had every right to call himself the strongest fighter in the Volakian Empire. A mere ripple of his strength would have been enough to kill most people. If Wilhelm had dodged every blow perfectly, they would still take a toll on his stamina, and even he was getting worn down.

Even without factoring Kurgan into the equation, the situation was overwhelmingly bad for Wilhelm-and for the entire squadron of the kingdom’s forces, in fact.

As he opened some distance and tried to reset his position, Wilhelm took a glance down the main avenue. While he and Kurgan battled, the scrum between the city guard, controlled by the Evil Eye, and Zergev Squadron, led chiefly by Bordeaux, was intensifying. The members of the squadron were forced to fight with one hand tied behind their backs to avoid killing fellow subjects of the kingdom-but he couldn’t let that choice drive them to give up their lives.

“If and when the moment calls for it, the young man will make his decision, I have no doubt. Wilhelm, you focus on your enemy.”

Another glance, and there was Pivot, standing beside Wilhelm as he tried to catch his breath. The phantom was right. The smart play was to leave it to Bordeaux to do what had to be done if worst came to worst. At this moment, the one Wilhelm had to defeat was Kurgan, right there in front of him.

“I see you have been hexed by the Evil Eye,” Kurgan said.

“What?” Wilhelm blinked, surprised by the gravelly voice.

Kurgan folded the four of his arms not holding cleavers in front of his chest, his terrible visage fixed on Wilhelm-no, on the ghost of Pivot beside him.

Surely, he couldn’t actually see Pivot. But he had observed Wilhelm’s monologue, the movements of his eyes, and had perhaps guessed the truth. Maybe it helped he was in the same camp as the Evil Eye user who had caused Wilhelm to start seeing this phantom.

Whatever it was, Kurgan could tell Wilhelm was ensnared by the Evil Eye.

“The Evil Eye of Ostentation causes its victims to see a reality at odds with what actually exists. It confronts those tormented by guilt with their own sins. Stride considered her worthy of making her his wife, but I must admit to some disappointment that the Sword Devil would be taken in by such tricks.”

“Disappointment?”

“A loss of faith, yes, Sword Devil. The remonstrations of the Evil Eye should entrap only the weak.”

The disappointment of the god of war, in a way, struck at Wilhelm’s heart more than any of Stride’s mockery. This was the second time in Wilhelm’s life that he had been deemed weak. The first time, Theresia had said it to him over her shoulder when she had revealed she was the Sword Saint in order to protect him. He had never forgotten the sense of powerlessness he’d felt at that moment. He thought he had killed his weakness. So why did the shadow of it still dog his path?

Could it be that Wilhelm Trias, by becoming Wilhelm van Astrea, had brought something with him that he ought not?

If so, then for him to be strong enough to defeat Eight-Arms once again, he would have to…

“Yes, good. That’s good.Thatis what makes you-”

“This makes me-”

Wilhelm strengthened his grip on his sword then looked up, as if guided, at Pivot. If the phantom was Wilhelm’s own sense of guilt, if it was a manifestation of his weakness, and if the only way he could be rid of it was by stepping over the corpse he had already passed by once-

Pivot silently returned Wilhelm’s gaze. He clasped his hands behind his back and made no move for the sword at his hip, just waited for the answer.

And Wilhelm…

“Don’t you underestimate my Captain Killer, you eight-armed bastard!”

The great shout tore through the tense air and stole away Wilhelm’s resolve. It came from Bordeaux, surrounded by guards on all sides, soaked in blood and wielding his halberd.

He wasn’t the only one in rough shape. Every member of the soldiers charging through the melee bore their share of wounds. Each of them was covered in blood, and each looked more than ready to continue the battle.

As Bordeaux stood in the center of it all, festooned with blood, he gave a smile like a mad dog and said, “How long do you think I spent making that idiot human shape up?! I ain’t gonna stand here and listen while you try to turn him back into a beast with some bullshit quibbling!”

Bordeaux slammed the butt of his halberd against the street, leaning on it to right himself, then brandished it at Kurgan and howled. The noise made Kurgan’s eyes widen ever so slightly, and then Bordeaux turned to Wilhelm. “You don’t have to hold back, Wilhelm. There’s nothing to keep you from holding your chin up high! No matter what you’re carrying, you are the kingdom’s sword, the kingdom’s strongest! Am I wrong?!”

“Sir! No sir!” the knights bellowed in answer. They lifted their weapons to the heavens. Worn down from attempting to fight through the city guard without killing anyone, they trusted Wilhelm and his sword to bust open the situation. They trusted their lives to him.

It was like the exact opposite of the beliefs that had been supporting Wilhelm until just that moment.

Pivot broke the silence and Wilhelm’s reverie with a question.“Is this the proof that your strength is in being the Sword Devil who threw away everything?”Wilhelm glanced at him and saw that his expression was no longer cold and detached-he was smiling. A smile Wilhelm didn’t remember seeing from Pivot in life. One more feature of a “ghost” that catered to Wilhelm’s needs, perhaps.

“You practically had me cornered with silence, and now you’re just going to flip over like that?”

“Cornered? Heavens. I never meant to corner you. You’re just as bad as you ever were at hearing people all the way through.”Pivot shrugged in fond exasperation. Now that was a gesture Wilhelm recognized from him.“Don’t you remember how I lost my life before your very eyes?”

“Yeah. How could I forget?”

“To you, it must’ve come as a bolt from the blue. At the time, I doubt you could imagine anyone letting themselves be cut down in your place on the battlefield.”

This man had done precisely that unimaginable thing, standing before the strongest warrior among the forces of evil and taking a mortal blow to protect Wilhelm. Even now, Wilhelm had dreams about it.

“Wilhelm, now it’s your turn,” Pivot said once again.

They were like the words of a spell, of a curse. As Pivot had died, now Wilhelm should do the same. But as Pivot spoke the words, he smiled not as if they were a curse, but a blessing.

“It’s your turn to risk your life for what matters most to you.”

Wilhelm’s breath caught. Abruptly, he took the sword in his hand-and slammed the hilt against his forehead. He felt and heard the shock run through him, and blood dribbled from the split skin.

“Wilhelm van Astrea, Sword Devil who desired to live as steel. Much death attends the path you walk-as it has, as it shall. Yet just the same, you must never stop walking.”

Wilhelm wiped the blood away with his sleeve, then gritted his teeth hard and faced forward.

“As the former vice-captain of Zergev Squadron, those are the words I wish to convey to the current captain. That’s everything.”“It’s plenty,” Wilhelm said.

“May you triumph in your battle. And please…take care of the young man for me.”

Wilhelm took a step forward. Pivot, who had been standing beside him, did not follow.

Of course not. He wasn’t actually there. The dead could not follow in the steps of those who were still alive.

As he had done before, he saw the Sword Devil go off to carve a swathe along the front. And then…

“Sorry to keep you waiting. Shall we go again?” Wilhelm said.

Kurgan paused. “I see you have discovered a faith slightly tangent to my hopes. But still…”

“Yeah. I don’t think it’s quite what you were talking about.”

Wilhelm and Kurgan closed in on each other once more, measuring how far their weapons would reach.

Kurgan had offered Wilhelm a great deal of his insight, but it was the advice and warning of a war god-what he thought was good to say.

So it was that Eight-Arms regarded the newly inspired Sword Devil not with disappointment, but with joy. Kurgan, Bordeaux and the soldiers, Pivot

-all of them had staked a great many dreams upon Wilhelm. But now… “Now I can go toe-to-toe with you without any baggage.” Kurgan watched him silently.

“I’m not about to lose this one.”

One could hardly say the situation had taken a turn in Wilhelm’s favor. Theresia was still in the hands of the enemy, Carol was still Stride’s puppet, and he didn’t know if Roswaal and Grimm were safe, nor how long Bordeaux and the others could hold out.

Yet just the same, because he now carried not one thing he did not need, the Sword Devil could bellow with all the might of the man who’d shouted as

if spitting blood, “Protect the kingdom to the end!”

“Yaaaaahh!” came the answering cry from the Mad Dog and his soldiers as they wrung out every last ounce of strength.

The Sword Devil smiled, and Eight-Arms smiled, and so began the longest moment the strongest of the Kingdom and the strongest of the Empire would share.

4

She had been stabbed through the belly, heat welling up as she dropped to her knees.

Her body had moved of its own volition. What a foolish mistake. What a stupid thing she had done.

She couldn’t die. She’d sworn to herself that was the one thing she absolutely, positively could not do. And here she had let that vow be swept away by her emotions, and thrown herself into the fight like this.

Ahh, yes, but…still. Still, I… Even so…

“Julia!”

She heard someone scream her former name. That made her smile.

Somewhere deep in her heart, a place that had been empty was now full as she was overcome by relief.

She had one thought:I’m glad I kept her safe.

It was the only thing that Roswaal J Mathers-

As Roswaal smiled, and Carol screamed and wept, Grimm Fauzen felt his heart burn hot in his chest. He held Carol’s weapon fast, while Roswaal had tied up the shinobi who would have ambushed them. Just now, there was no one to stop an attack on the walking disaster.

“Hrrooohhh!” Grimm howled, stamping down with his foot and kicking his great shield up into the air. At that moment, he looked past Carol and Roswaal, the two women, and locked eyes with Stride.

He had put all his energy into that kick, and it sent the shield hurtling toward the defenseless disaster.

The spinning silver platter was a hunk of metal as heavy as a human torso. If it connected with someone’s body, it could easily smash them to pieces- and it was heading straight at Stride where he stood on the edge of the rooftop.

“My lord!”

One of the shinobi, Shasuke, tried to cross the shadows in an attempt to defeat the attack, but he faltered. Roswaal, her belly pierced, had grabbed his arm and would not let him go.

“My,” she said with an alluring smile, “tearing up a girl’s stomach… Hoooow cruel.”

The blood had drained from her smiling face, but it was enough to fatally interfere with the shinobi’s attempt to reach his master. The huge shield closed in on Stride with no one to stop it, closer, ever closer, approaching the one who had declared he had no strength to fight. He would never be able to avoid it.

“Pfah!” Stride clicked his tongue, but it was drowned out by the clang of an impact of metal.

With a dull thud, Grimm’s shield hit the rooftop and rolled along. It had been knocked down by a mysterious sword Stride had drawn from thin air-a jeweled blade of crimson that shined with a great light.

“The Sunlight Blade Volakia, passed down in the Empire of Volakia,” Roswaal said, blood dripping from her mouth as she finished Grimm’s thought.

Grimm knitted his brow at the name, then realized that it was the heirloom, the sword of absolute power. He began to scowl as he realized Stride had been lying about being unable to fight.

Yet as Grimm watched, caution written on his face, something difficult to believe happened. Stride’s left arm, the one whose hand bore the sword, burst into flame.

“Hrrnngh…! Why, you…!” Stride’s face contorted in agony, and the Sunlight Blade dropped from his burning hand. Before it even hit the rooftop, it vanished just as it had come, into thin air. The flames tormenting Stride, however, did not disappear, but sought to consume him.

“Forgive my disrespect, sire!” Shasuke cried, and then before the flames could reach Stride’s torso, the shinobi jumped at him and sliced off his arm. It tumbled to the ground, where it burned until it was nothing but a pile of blackened cinders.

The shinobi’s quick thinking had saved Stride’s life by a hair. He crossed his remaining arm in front of his chest and exhaled.

“So I unexpectedly lose an arm. And what’s more…”

He raised his foot and stomped on the blackened limb. Then he scratched at some carbonized bits and kicked them away, furious. They were his rings, unable to retain their shape in the heat. The five rings on his left hand that had

been so crucial to the Ten Proud Commandments. Meaning…

“I won’t be dancing toyourtune anymore,” came a loud, clear voice that resounded around the rooftop.

It came from Carol, who had her freedom back and was cradling the collapsed Roswaal. She turned her blazing, clear eyes upon Stride, then spoke to Roswaal, who lay in her arms. “Lady Mathers! If you can hear me, just hang on, please! Lady Mathers!”

As she shouted, Carol whipped off her cloak and wrapped it around the wound in Roswaal’s belly, which was still oozing blood profusely. The cloak quickly grew heavy with blood, but it didn’t stop the bleeding.

It didn’t stop Roswaal’s life from leaking out of her.

“Please, Lady Mathers, open your eyes… Please, just open your eyes!” Carol’s voice quavered helplessly. But her eyes widened when she felt a touch on her cheek.
