“Did you…call me Julia…or did I…mishear?” Roswaal had just managed to open her eyes, although it was all she could do to keep them that way. She’d removed the glove from her left hand and touched Carol’s cheek, and a gentle-but all too ephemeral-smile hovered on her face. “I’d be juuuust as pleased…if you didn’t…cry, Carol. You…always look…in such pain…”

“Oh…”

“You’re quick to get angry…but really…a smile is what suits you best,” Roswaal said between gasps for breath. Carol forced back her tears and tried to smile-but failed. She was able to wipe the failure off her face, try again, and this time, she managed it. Her eyes were red and puffy from weeping. and she was never going to fool anyone into thinking she hadn’t been crying. Yet even so, Carol smiled, just as this person she cared so much about had asked.

Then she said, “If I… If I call you Julia, will you tease me like you always do? Please?”

“Yeah…yeah, that would be good. I’d like that.” A smile came over Roswaal’s pale face, and she nodded several times. She’d seen what she wanted to see. Then she turned her multicolored eyes, lit with a flickering love, and said, “There’s a butler in my house, a man named Clind. Tell him to take care of Karl…”

“N-no! No, you can’t do this! Please, Lady M-”

“Julia.” Roswaal put a finger to Carol’s lips to stop her tearful shouts.

Carol was taken aback by the sensation but then seemed to cling to it.

“Julia, please…”

A single tear traced a path down her cheek.

Roswaal-no, Julia-caught it lovingly on her finger. “Be happy,” she said. “Be happy with Grimm.”

“Julia?”

With those last words, like a prayer, the weight in Carol’s arms seem to get heavier. Yet at the same time, it was as if something had left her embrace.

“Julia? Julia… Julia, Julia, Julia!”

Julia’s head fell to the side, and all the strength deserted her body. And not only the strength. Something more important-the most important thing of all -went with it, never again to return.

“Jul-”

“So she’s dead-in the middle of all this.” The voice was dreadfully dry but carried with it no hint of sarcasm or mockery. Stride, missing his left arm, gazed down where Julia slept in Carol’s arms. His expression was cold, a welter of emotions playing through his eyes. What was really in his heart, no one could guess.

Except that, somewhere in those emotions, Carol thought she caught a glimpse of loneliness and envy.

“Don’t you dare.”

The moment Carol saw those things, her anger reached the boiling point.

She had just lost someone-someone she treasured had been stolen from her. “Death would be too good for you, Stride.”

“Yes, perhaps. I, myself, would find it hard to bear if my end were the same as that of common men.”

Carol refused to listen to his jabbering anymore. She took a deep breath, forcing herself to contain her raging emotions.

First, she slid Julia’s limp body onto the ground, crossing the hands over the chest. She gently wiped away the blood that had dribbled from the woman’s lips, straightened the hair over her forehead-and then stood up.

With her knight’s blade in hand, Carol stood beside her lover, who had retrieved his great shield, and with her friend behind her, she faced the enemy.

“My lord, I believe this will be the moment of truth.”

“The spell that bound you has burned to ashes. For what reason do you stay here? Did you not share a wish with your worthless little brother to send my head flying from my shoulders and tear my heart out of my chest should the slightest opportunity present itself?”

“I am the little brother, Shasuke, sire. My older brother Raizo is his own creature. Further, my lord, we are determined to stand with you until the end, spell or no spell.”

“Hmph,” Stride snorted, his arrogance undimmed by Shasuke’s show of loyalty. Why would Shasuke seek to obey such a destructive man as him?

“Some may be saved by the dazzling light of the sun. Others are saved by poisonous filth,” Shasuke said. “I do not ask for your understanding. I simply speak of what is.”

“When the master is wrong, the servant should take steps to correct him,” Carol replied. “But that’s enough out of you. I’ll hear no more-”

“She’s right. There is no more value in bending our ear to your words,” Stride said, stealing Carol’s thunder as she was about to make her move.

What really threw her, however, was not his cruel words-it was something he pulled from the folds of his clothing and held high. When she saw it, Carol was speechless, and Grimm likewise opened his eyes wide in shock.

It was a book, a single volume with a black cover. Stride held it aloft as though it were deeply important, but the cover bore no title, and at a glance it was impossible to guess what might be within. Yet they knew immediately what it was.

It was the symbol of absolute evil, which should have been possessed only by the chosen ones…

“There is no call for any unnecessary words, no? But this is just the same. The Sword Saint and the Holy Dragon, the Kingdom and the Empire, blessing and curse: The value of all things and the span of all things is riddled with traces of the observers in heaven and their will. Thus I offer no objection to them. This is the proof there is no pawn that does no harm, no game board that does not break.”

“What…what are you saying, you bastard! Stride, you son of a bitch!”

“I have not even the scantest faith in the Witch, but for the one who offered me this book and authority… For that diligent student who gave guidance on how to wield the Ten Proud Commandments-I shall now speak.”

“I am the Witch Cult’s Archbishop of Pride-Stride Volakia!”

“The Witch Cult?! And…you take the name Volakia?”

“Sadly, it’s simply a happenstance connection between the Witch Factor and the manifestation of power. Unlike that diligent student, I have no intention of worshiping the Witch of Jealousy. Then again, the Witch is something of a threat to the observers themselves…so perhaps she is on my side after all.”

The edges of Stride’s lips raised sarcastically, and Carol’s thoughts went everywhere at once. The Witch Cult and the Volakian Empire… If they were both part of Stride’s machinations…

“Cyaaaol,” said Grimm, tapping her on the shoulder and nodding at her.

“Wee kill th’s guy. Juss one more r’son to do i’.”

“Yes,” Carol said slowly. “Yes, you’re right.”

Those words alone were enough to bring her some relief, and the chaos in her head subsided. At this moment, they should be concerned with the safety of the kingdom, with defeating the enemy leader, and most of all with…

“My name is Carol Remendes. My family is the scabbard that has served House Astrea for generations. But for this one moment-”

She stood with her sword at the ready, and memories flashed through her mind of all the times the other woman had confounded her. Of all the times she’d made her mad. Of all the times they had laughed together. How much Carol had loved her.

So now, for this one moment, Carol fought not as a daughter of the Remendes line.

“As Julia’s friend, I, Carol, will strike you down!”

“Bold words from a woman who could not shake off my curse. Nothing to add from her little friend?”

“No’hing,” was all Grimm said.

Stride raised an eyebrow. “Hoh.”

Grimm’s face was set. He showed neither anger nor hatred but regarded Stride with an unshakable sense of duty. “Yoh’re juss anot’er villain I happ’nd to run across.”

“Magnificent!” Stride smiled from the bottom of his heart at this exchange.

Carol concluded she might never understand him if she had all eternity to try.

With that, she stood side by side with Grimm, ready for the fight, sword and shield standing together. Shasuke clasped blades in both his hands, ready to protect the grinning Stride.

The two sides charged at each other-but someone else was even quicker.

There was a tremendous howl, and the black dragon, which had broken free of Stride’s spells, swallowed the spire, the symbol of Pictat, with a blast of its breath.

5

She ran and she ran. The world seemed to have no end.

If this was indeed a place born of her sense of guilt, then perhaps it was only natural it should go on forever. For after all, a sin once committed could never truly be forgiven and atoned for.

“How pessimistic…!”

Theresia swept away the thought as it came into her head and kept running, her breath coming in gasps. She could shake off the horde of pursuing dead but never really escape them. They would circle around ahead of her as if they knew where she was. They gave her no time to so much as rest.

Then again, she never used to feel tired, no matter how long or how far she ran.

“Even here, my belly feels heavy, my stamina is flagging, and I don’t sense my blessing…”

Theresia spotted some rocky crags and dove among them, putting her hand against the wall and taking stock of her condition.

Between her pregnancy, the loss of her blessings, and the relative laxity of her days since she had retired, spending her time absorbed in the life of a newlywed, her strength was nowhere near what it had once been.

There would be no point if she simply went on like this, letting the child in her belly get mixed up in everything that was going on and leaving herself trapped by the Evil Eye. Melinda was Stride’s wife and the key to his plans- if Theresia could destroy her Evil Eye…

“It would have to help Wilhelm and the others fighting outside!”

As it was with blessings, so it was with many forms of special power: The possessor’s mental state had a significant influence on that power. The effect of the Evil Eye was immense, but if it could be undone, then the foundation of Stride’s plot would become a brittle sword, ready to snap.

That had been Theresia’s objective, but so far, it had only gotten her more trapped, pulled deeper into the plot.

“Without my sword…I really am just a weak woman.”

While she stood contemplating, the people whom Theresia had killed closed in, calling for her to join them.

Seeing the faces of the deceased, hearing the pain in their voices, Theresia thought that her disappointment earlier had gone beyond arrogance to be almost inhuman. Even if she had still possessed the Sword Saint’s blessing, could she have cut them down again? Could she kill those who had already died once? Did she truly seek to return to a life steeped in blood?

In a world that gave shape to sin, the dead who were the symbol of her guilt cursed Theresia, the sinner, and closed in, seeking to mete out a punishment appropriate to what she had done. Closer, ever closer…

“…Ah!”

Had she been too lost in thought? Or perhaps she, in fact, wished for punishment?

Very suddenly, Theresia found her craggy hideout surrounded on all sides by the dead. There was nowhere to run; she was cornered.

She looked this way and that but saw no avenue of escape. She put her hands to her belly, her lips trembling. “Wilhelm…” No. He wasn’t here.

“Carol…”

No. She wasn’t here.

“Someone… Anyone!”

No. There was no one here. Theresia was completely alone. All alone in this place. “Help me…Father!”

“Yes. Yes, of course I will.”

Her frail cry for help was met by an embrace so sweet it made her want to cry.

“Wha?” Theresia murmured, and at that moment, several brilliant flashes of sword strokes fell upon the dead who had been about to tear her limb from limb, scattering them.

Theresia’s blue eyes widened when she saw the men armed with knights’ blades who had saved her.

There was no way they should have been here.

“Now, you really mustn’t steal a father’s thunder like that!”

“C’mon! We were just as worried about Theresia as you were!”

“What?! You’d argue the point with me here?!”

The voice of the man embracing Theresia nearly cracked as he answered the others.

Theresia had heard this banter before, and recognized the warmth of the exchange. She shook her head vigorously. No-this wasn’t right. This couldn’t be. This couldn’t be happening.

“You carry too great a burden, big sister. I know you hate having killed so many people as the Sword Saint, but don’t ever think that we are part of your guilt.”

“’Course, it’s because of the way you like to carry us around that we were able to be here!”

She recognized the sources of the two voices. One of them a kindly face, the other a virile young man who casually draped his sword across his shoulders.

“Cajiress… Carlan… My brothers…”

“Don’t forget, I’m here, too, Theresia.”

“Thames? Even you?”

It was her younger brother, Cajiress, and her second oldest brother, Carlan. And there, flexing his biceps, was a young man who looked so much like her father, but whose bold attitude made him so very different. Her eldest brother, Thames.

She had lost her three brothers in the Demi-human War, never expecting to see them again.

“This is a miracle wrought by love. Don’t you think so, Theresia?”

“Father, what are you talking about?”

“Wha?! Everything that just happened, andthat’syour attitude? I thought you would be overjoyed!”

This flummoxed reaction, needless to say, came from her beloved father, Veltol. Theresia stuck out her tongue and said, “I was just being funny,” then buried her face in his chest.

She felt tears well up in her eyes. It was no mistake. She had, in fact, been able to meet them here.

“Dad… You’re…”

“You must not blame yourself, Theresia. The same goes for Carol. Neither you nor she have done a single thing to deserve blame.”

“But…but there were so many things I still wanted to talk to you about…”

“Believe me, I know the feeling of unfinished business. I wanted to hold my first grandchild and to attend Carol’s wedding one day. I was going to make this year’s anniversary with Tishua the grandest of our lives, and I had hoped to share a drink with young Wilhelm sometime soon. What’s more…”

As Veltol counted his regrets on his fingers, Theresia found she couldn’t hold back the tears.

She’d wanted those things, too. She’d wanted them for him. But the chance would never come. The business would remain unfinished, forever… “But Theresia, listen to me. That’s all right,” her father said.

“Wha…?”

“No life ends without some things left undone. No one can do absolutely everything they wish for. And why? Because I lived in bliss and died in bliss

-and in a happy human life, there is no end to wanting. If I finished the business I have now, I would only find another wish to hold fast and look forward to. I always would, without end.” Veltol puffed out his chest and said, “Theresia, the important thing is, we love you. What we could not do will pass down to you, and to your child, and to that child’s child. And that’s a good thing.”

“Dad…”

“So don’t mind if we stretch ourselves a bit to make sure you can do that for us. Isn’t that right, boys?”

Veltol raised his head, and the look on his face was indeed gallant. His three sons turned back toward him and said…

“Hey, Dad! While you’ve been chatting,we’vebeen busy!”

“Yeah, and you can’t wield a sword to save your life, so we’re the only ones ‘stretching’ ourselves!”

“Whaaa?! Is that how you talk to your father?! If that’s how you’re going to be, boys, then I won’t bring my special ultimate helper!”

Even as Theresia and Veltol had been talking, Veltol’s sons had been busy slicing up the oncoming dead, and they were not terribly impressed with their father. Theresia, however, with Veltol’s hands on her shoulders, cocked her head and asked, “Helper?” She couldn’t imagine who could be more help than the salvation she’d already received.

“That would be me, Theresia. Although, I can’t say I’m very happy about it.”

The answer to her question was accompanied by the flash of a sword from someone new who danced down onto the battlefield. He laid low a whole horde of the dead at a stroke, and he had long hair and a slim frame-too slim. He looked somehow lonely.

“Uncle Freibel…!”

“Freibel van Astrea, the former Sword Saint, hides his shame and presents himself on the field.” The man rested his sword against his shoulder, smiling so subtly that one could almost miss it. Freibel van Astrea was the former Sword Saint and Veltol’s younger brother by blood.

Theresia had inherited her blessing of the Sword Saint from him-so on more than one occasion, she’d had cause to resent her uncle for the cruel destiny that the blessing had brought with it.

“I make no pretension to atone for saddling you with that burden,” Freibel said. “It was unavoidable that you would take on that responsibility eventually.”

“Yes, Uncle,” Theresia said after a moment. “I know. At the time, I wasn’t able to do my duty.”

“That’s right. You ran from it, and I presume there are lives that were lost

in exchange. If that is a sin, then so be it. However…”

Amid this incredible meeting, the mass of the dead continued to attack relentlessly. Freibel didn’t even bother to turn around but sent them flying with a tremendous blow-though, it pained Theresia deep inside to see the dead being cut down a second time.

“However, do not blame yourself. This may be a world forged by your sense of guilt, but these are not the very lives you took. Your guilt is misplaced.”

“You sound just like you used to, Uncle …”

“I understand your desire to believe that what you’ve done is a sin. But if that be so, then what does that make me? What does that make Thames, or your other brothers who have come to help you?”

Theresia fell silent at the question, pondering. Just beside her, Veltol was not looking very pleased, but she didn’t even notice him.

What was Theresia’s uncle trying to communicate to her? She considered the question intently. After all, she’d never had such a chance to speak so frankly with him in his life.

“This place is not the abyss of your sins,” Freibel said. “This is a world given shape by what the bewitched person wishes to believe. It was a kind heart, a kind person, who formed this place.”

“A…kind person…”

“Do not drown here in your guilt, Theresia. I cannot let you die in this place. Nothing is atoned for by death. Instead, you must live.”

With that, Freibel stood in front of Theresia and Veltol, covering them, and launched a strike against the horde of the dead. Thames and the others stood with him, forming an impregnable line.

How heartening, to have them there. Was it the very lack of the Sword Saint’s blessing that allowed her to even have the thought? Was it the product of the whims of the Sword God, who before had mercilessly ignored Theresia’s brothers as they devoted themselves to the blade?

“There’s so much I want to say…,” Veltol began, but then paused, and looked at the Astrea men as if at something impossibly radiant. There was injury in his eyes, the yearning of a man who had not been blessed with any gift for the sword.

But it was soon gone, replaced by compassion in the blue eyes that looked down at Theresia. “Freibel is quite right. Theresia, you must live. Don’t carry this guilt around with you. In fact, your father is surprised you cornered yourself quite so thoroughly.”

“I didn’t realize it had gotten…quite this bad,” Theresia answered. Now that it had been given concrete form, she could only say that her awareness of her own feelings had been too dim.

Veltol put his hand on his daughter’s shoulder, the girl who held this deep darkness within her, and smiled. “I’m not telling you to forget your guilt. But I do want you to stop letting it rule your life. There is no need to liveonlyto atone. If, just the same, your heart still aches…then repay the debt you owe.”

“The…debt?”

“Live, not to atone for sins committed, but to repay kindness done. Live in bliss and die in bliss. That is what I want for my daughter.”

He smiled broadly, and Theresia’s eyes went wide. Was such a life permitted to the line of the Sword Saints? Was such a gentle way of being possible for the Astreas, compelled to act as the sword of the kingdom? Veltol Astrea, for one, was smiling: He had done it.

“Dad…”

“Mm?”

“The baby in my belly… I wanted you to name it.”

“Ah… I see. Yes, yes, I hear you.”

At Theresia’s little request, Veltol’s smile grew even wider. He ran a hand through his shock of red hair, the same color as Theresia’s, and said, “Well, then, I suppose I’d better give it a good deal of thought.”

“Of course, Dad. It’s a promise.”

A promise they would never be able to keep, Theresia knew, even as she made it.

Then she took her father’s arm and turned once more toward the Astrea men before them.

“Thames, Carlan, Cajiress, Uncle Freibel,” she said, calling their names, and one by one they turned to look at her.

Theresia took in their faces, took in the sight of them holding back the waves of the dead, burning the vision into her mind’s eye. Though they could not relax their defenses for even an instant, they nonetheless showed their strongest side to her, that she might never see them in weakness.

It brought home to Theresia that she had always been protected like this.

“I love all of you,” she said. “I love you so much.”

As she conveyed her love to her family, she wondered if she was able to give them a real smile. She wondered if she was able to be the Theresia Astrea her father, her uncle, her brothers older and younger had known so well, back before she received the “sword-name” of van. Just Theresia Astrea.

And she wondered if the smiles they each gave her in the end were the true answer to her question.

6

There was a sound like breaking glass, the signal of destruction.

“Ahh…hah…”

For an instant, Theresia put her hands to her chest and curled into a ball at the pain of not having been breathing. Again and again, she sucked in the dusty air that greeted her as she returned.

And there…

“Ah-ahhhh! Ahhh! My…my Eye! You broke the spell?!”

Melinda’s cry came shortly after Theresia’s return to consciousness. She was covering her eyes with both hands, then raced to the window in a panic and looked outside. There, she clawed at her ashen hair and yowled again.

“This can’t be! This can’t be! No, no, no, no nooooo!” “Melinda?” Theresia asked.

“My Evil Eye of Ostentation is broken… What about my lord’s wish? What about his ambitions?! Ahh!”

Still stricken by confusion, Melinda suddenly seemed to have a thought. She turned back toward Theresia, who had heaved herself into a sitting position and was looking at her. Both eyes closed, Melinda advanced on her. She stretched out her hands, clutching Theresia’s shoulders and bringing her face right up to Theresia’s. Realizing what she was about to do, Theresia cried “No!” and tried to push the woman away.

“Hnngh!”

Theresia was too late. Melinda’s eyes opened, and she was once again confronted with the Evil Eye. The next instant, however, Melinda lurched back as if struck by an electric shock and slumped to her knees. Blood began to dribble from her eyes, and the spiderweb pattern within them gradually turned red.

“What?! No, no, don’t push yourself so hard!” Theresia exclaimed.

“Don’t-don’t touch me, please!” Melinda yelped, batting away Theresia’s hand when she reached out to hold her up. “You…did that on purpose… But how?”

Theresia was quiet for a moment. “My family sent me back here. They told me not to cling to my guilt.”

Melinda looked at the ground as tears of blood poured from her eyes. She was profoundly regretful. She knew Theresia had deliberately provoked her to use the Evil Eye, so that she might have a chance to break the bewitchment of the guards in the city below. It would have been one thing had Stride given her instructions on the matter, but Melinda could have never imagined such a plan on her own. Theresia was sure her uncle had been right.

“I know you really did care for my baby,” Theresia said. “Let’s stop this.

No more.”

“I ca…”

“You can’t do that? No, that’s not true. Right now, I don’t have my sword, don’t have my blessing. I’m just a mother. Just a woman. If you have someone you love, as I do…”

Theresia could neither understand nor even allow for the possibility of the humanity of Stride, whom Melinda loved and supported. But that did not mean Theresia had to reject Melinda.

Melinda was silent for a long moment. She kept her eyes closed, looking first up and then down, over and over. At length, however, she seemed to come to some sort of decision.

Spotting a ray of hope, Theresia said, “Yes, that’s right,” and tried to take the woman’s hand… “Wha?”

…except at the same instant, Melinda shoved Theresia as hard as she could, sending Theresia sprawling. Theresia could only lay there, blinking in shock.

Just then, there was a tremendous noise above them, and the black dragon’s breath enveloped the spire, sending a conflagration pouring into their room.

7

A shinobi was a warrior created through a process of torment, forged in the agonies of hell.

First, your name was taken from you. Then your family, your possessions, your past, your future-everything from before you became a shinobi was stripped away, your life wiped to a clean slate. Only then were you the raw material fit for shaping.

What followed was training, drugs, spells, and every awful method from every age and corner of the world. Only one out of a hundred candidates refrained from killing themselves, and of each hundred of those, only one emerged mentally intact. Of each hundred of those, only one survived the training, and only one of each hundred who survived emerged a complete shinobi.

As such, Raizo and Shasuke, twin brothers who had completed the process together, were a new thing in the shinobi village, an unparalleled work of art, and much was expected of their future careers.

The adults in the village should have realized, however, thatastwin brothers, Raizo and Shasuke had been unfit to be shinobi from the very first stages of the selection process.

In the end, therefore, the “twin warriors,” who had sometimes been called the village’s crowning masterwork, went from house to house, slaughtering all the adults who had taken everything from them, and all those who were their allies. Thereafter, the pair became fugitives.

Even as they hunted their pursuers, Raizo and Shasuke knew that they couldn’t live on the run for long. And yet, though their lives were not bound to last long, there was equally no reason to end them early. Perhaps that was why they did what they did.

“I shall put you to the grandest use before I cast you aside.”

As invitations went, this one was neither kind nor just-and both brothers accepted it.

Their true wish was to serve someone with grand ambitions, however absurd his goal might be. The one, the only one, who used the fugitive twin warriors as the shinobi they were was the man who would be quietly criticized by many: Stride Volakia.

So even now, as the world was ending…

“My lord!”

As the black dragon’s fiery breath came at them, Shasuke grabbed Stride and lunged into the air.

An instant later, the spire was smashed by a wave of heat, consumed by literal firepower undreamt of. The blast wind scorched Shasuke’s skin, and he knew those who had not escaped must be dead.

But a voice tickled his ear, a quiet rasp of rage: “You fool-where do you think you’re going?!”

Shasuke twisted in midair, only to be met by a sword stroke he was unable to avoid. It bit into his shoulder, sending him tumbling.

The woman fighter with golden hair had pursued Shasuke into the very air -it was Carol.

He’d known her swordplay was excellent, but he had taken her for little more than that. Now she moved through the air as if walking on solid ground, striking the laden shinobi with a hail of blows.

“Stepping through the air ismytrick! You’ve made a grave miscalculation!” she said.

Shasuke hissed. “But if you’re here, then what of your beloved? What has become ofhim?!”

The roof had been seared by flame; only those who knew how to flee into the air had escaped. And unlike Shasuke, who carried Stride in his arms, Carol did not bear her lover with her.

An ordinary man with nothing but an oversized shield? He could never have survived.

Stride, from Shasuke’s arms, was looking over his shoulder and said in a voice full of heat, “That is exactlywhyhe survived, simpleton.”

Shasuke followed his master’s gaze, which was fixed upon the roof, where the last heat of the blaze still lingered.

A great shield shone on the rooftop. It was the ordinary man, who had deflected the heat and protected the body of the dead beauty.

“I am the scabbard and Grimm is the shield-the people who stand ever with the sword as its friends!”

Parrying the flashing sword strike with hiskunai, Shasuke was pushed back, but he found a place to land: on the back of the black dragon.

The creature roared. It was tens of meters long, so the weight of one puny human meant nothing to it. Free of the spell of the rings, the dragon bellowed and howled. Meanwhile, the shinobi and the swordswoman battled across the supernatural monster’s back, its wings, and its arms, exchanging blows like a story out of a dream.

The dragon twisted under their feet, its claws and tail slashing mercilessly at the air. A single blow from the creature could kill either of them instantly. Shasuke gritted his teeth and braced himself against the whipping winds. Cradling his master with his wounded left arm, he used the right to fight a first-rate swordswoman. He, who had been forged as the ultimate warrior, demonstrated all his skill as they conducted a running battle across a creature that could have been something out of a joke-or a legend.

Do such things happen?Canthey happen?

Could a shinobi, who was meant to lurk in the shadows of history, the dark corners of the world, the unseen background of stories, ever hidden, ever chased off, wasting away in the darkness-could such a person stand tall on this open stage? “Hngha!”

Shasuke bared his teeth and spat out a breath. No, helaughed.

Shasuke, who had been raised forever being told to throw away his emotions and shutter his heart-Shasuke, who along with his brother Raizo had failed to become a shinobi and had become a fugitive instead-laughed for the first time in ages.

He was glad now he had cursed his destiny and joined hands with the ploys of a man who sought to destroy the world.

“Ahhh, all you gods, but this has been good!” he cried. He laughed again, and then blindingly fast, he drove his blade at Carol’s pale neck. But the greatest single strike of Shasuke’s life was nothing before the technique of the Sword Devil, the kingdom’s strongest.

How, then, could the shield bearer who had observed that technique from up close for so many years fail to defend against it?

“Caaaol!” shouted the man who had jumped on the dragon’s back, risking his life for the sake of this single blow. He caught it with his shield, and without missing a beat, the woman kicked into the sky, raising her sword high above her head.

Shasuke let his shinobi art flow through his body, making his flesh as hard as steel. Yet he knew already his technique was powerless in the face of that gleaming blow.

“I wonder, did my older brother fulfill his role?”

The blow came down at an angle, cleaving through Shasuke’s right shoulder and exiting at his left hip, slicing him in two. Shasuke coughed blood, but even as he sustained the mortal blow, there was a broad smile on his face.

He only hoped his brother was smiling, too.

“My lord… I go before you…”

There, soaked in blood on the back of a three-headed dragon, Shasuke had a thought:

I may be the only shinobi who ever died such a grand death.

8

“Wanna know the truth? I don’t give two shits about the likes of you kids. And whoever you killed, they deserved it for not being strong enough to fight back… What, me? I’m a shinobi because…well. Somewhere, someday, I want a grand death, like a blooming flower. But don’t tell anyone, eh?”

Raizo and Shasuke had met the shinobi after they had destroyed their village and gone on the run. He was the strongest shinobi they had ever known, the one who had seen death closer than anyone, and the most mysterious.

The old shinobi was stronger than Raizo and Shasuke; the story of the twin warriors nearly ended right there. But by some whim or caprice he had seen fit to spare them, allowing them to go on to find Stride and accept his promise to use them up as shinobi-and that led them to this moment.

Why should he remember that strange shinobi just now?

Perhaps because he seemed likely to realize the shinobi’s ambition before the man himself did.

“After all, a man such as I plotted to assassinate the very king of Lugunica.”

And what a committed master he had found; how deep the man’s cruel little plans went.

By this point, Stride must be attempting his grand ambition. Kurgan and Melinda, and Shasuke too, must be fighting with the kingdom’s picked troops on the great stage known as Pictat. Raizo, however, was all but oblivious to that epic battle as he returned to the royal capital of Lugunica and snuck into the castle.

When they lost their Sword Saint, their Holy Dragon, and finally their king, there would no longer be anyone who clung to the comforting myth that had been the bedrock of the kingdom’s prosperity for so long.

Properly speaking, it would mean that Stride’s ambition, along with Raizo and the others who had served as his hands and feet, had changed the very course of the world through sheer brute force.

Silently, Raizo slipped from one shadow to another, as quickly as he could, into the royal castle. His sense of time had become badly distorted, but he knew it was halfway through the Hour of Fire, and that the king, Jionis Lugunica, would be taking a nap in his bedchamber.

Even now, Raizo was careful and thorough, sneaking above the ceiling of Jionis’s chambers. When he strained his ears, he could hear the gentle breathing of a man asleep. All he had to do was sneak into the room with all speed and snap his spine.

It was not Raizo’s style to make his victims suffer unnecessarily. Nonetheless, in order to dramatize the king’s death, he would probably have

to put the body somewhere more obvious…

“I perceive a most fearsome foe is afoot. I’m afraid I won’t be able to hold back in this case. You must pardon my impertinence.”

It was a voice he should not have heard, yet he was hearing it. No sooner had he heard the words than something wrapped itself around the right side of his body and began crushing it with immense force.

“Hnnghh…ahhh!”

Raizo twisted; he was being swallowed by the air itself. He abandoned his right arm and leg. As he heard and felt flesh and bone crushing and tearing away, he smashed through the ground underfoot and dropped into the bedchamber. He knew the right side of his body was totally mutilated, and the left only somewhat better. The wounds were mortal.

“That is…some skill… Perhaps you’d consider…becoming a shinobi?”

“I appreciate your generous estimation of me. However, I already serve a household. My apologies.”

With that, a man with blue hair dressed in a butler’s outfit jumped easily out of the bed. It bordered on insubordination for someone like him to sleep in the spot reserved for the king-but insofar as this was a plot to catch an assassin, it had worked beautifully.

“It was my dear wife’s idea. Master Miklotov gave it his approval, and

Master Orfeu helped set it up. Perfect.”

“Then Jionis Lugunica…?”

“Is in a safe location. Now, prepare yourself.”

Raizo realized then that any hope of him killing the king had vanished. Finding the missing monarch, getting past his guards, and taking the man’s life was no longer realistic.

There was a more fundamental problem, too. Raizo doubted the young man in front of him would let him leave so easily.

“I thought we had all the kingdom’s strongest fighters tied down… But you… Who are you?”

“No one worthy of so much as giving his name. I do, however, have something to tell you. A farewell.”

“And what would that be?”

“If you and yours seek to make an enemy of history, then I am also your enemy. For I am one who knows the era of the Witch from all those centuries ago. A point of reference.”

The young man made it sound so simple-and then, he bowed.

Death was near. Raizo’s breath smelled of blood. He savored the young man’s words and laughed. “A fine story to bring to Lord Stride when I meet him in hell.”

“Then give him your best hospitality. And to my wife’s soul, comfort, if you would. I thank you.”

Raizo did not follow the man’s logic, nor his reasoning. He only knew that the outcome was what he wished for, and so he prepared to fight.

He didn’t know this man’s name, but then, he had never asked that shinobi’s name, either. His own death might blossom in a way slightly different from that man’s grand imaginings, but still.

“My lord, I go before you.”

He would be able to die as one who had served a master who prioritized substance over form; as one who had struggled to break the mold of the world.

Raizo was taken by an unaccustomed jolt of brotherly feeling for Shasuke:

I’m sorry, he thought,to be the only one to achieve such a death.

9

“My lord… I go before you…”

With those words, the shinobi’s corpse tumbled off the back of the dragon, blood and gore scattering everywhere.

Carol hardly watched as her implacable foe’s body fell out of sight. She brought her sword to bear and prepared to continue the battle.

Before her was the man who called himself Bishop of the Deadly Sins, the man who, now stripped of his loyal bodyguard, clung to the back of the dragon against the whipping wind. The walking disaster, Stride Volakia.

“Looks like you’re out of ideas, you fiend,” Carol said. “The dragon has escaped your clutches, and all your plans are as froth upon the waves.”

“My, how you chirp and twitter now that the situation has changed. But I shall forgive you. It is the way of those with minor parts to change their tune every time the background music shifts.”

The burning away of his arm, the loss of his last allies, and the fact he couldn’t even stand up on the dragon’s back did nothing to dim Stride’s arrogance.

“Was it your inability to find ordinary happiness like other people that drove you to these lengths of violence?” Carol asked quietly.

“-What?”

For a second, he looked like a man whose lies had been pierced through. Then Carol’s determined face reflected in his eyes, and he looked at the ground. His shoulders began to quake, and a stifled noise came from his throat. He was laughing.

“Heh-heh-heh… Ha-ha-ha-ha! Hah… Ha-ha! You fool! You speak as a clown. Do you pity me? You have been by my side as I stood at the center of this drama, and is this all you have learned of me? How stupid must you be!”

“That’s right, I’m stupid. Because I’m stupid, I was caught up in your vile little plans, I lost the things I should have protected, and my friend is dead. You had me tricked at every turn, and I despise myself for it.” Carol looked at her bloodstained hands. She had allowed her irreplaceable friend to die, and she had laid hands on the man to whom she owed everything when she should have protected him-so many mistakes she had made. When she thought about it, she couldn’t shake the sense that she had done nothing but make mistakes since the day she had first met Theresia.

And yet, to her, to the stupid Carol Remendes, Grimm said… “Ahh…love yohh.”

Carol nodded to the man at her side, and a soft smile formed on her face. “Yes, and I love you, too. And Julia loved me. And Lord Veltol, he cherished me. As Lady Theresia loves me, as well.”

At that, the grin vanished from Stride’s face, along with the ridicule and mockery in his eyes. Instead, he let go of the dragon’s back and slowly rose to his feet.

He did not know how to fight. If he was not clinging to the dragon’s scales, then he had only seconds to stand there. In point of fact, he would soon lose his footing, and his body would be tossed into open space…

“I admit it,” he said. His face already looked as if it had forgotten that it had ever smiled, and he was being pushed back by the wind. As Carol and Grimm looked on in amazement he said, “You win-for now.”

“You thinknowyou can-!” Carol saw that Stride meant to destroy himself-and she meant to stop him. She kicked off the dragon’s back, racing forward.

Stride surrendered himself to the wind, but Carol caught up with him. She would not let him pass this judgment on himself. At the very least, she wanted a sword of the Astrea household to finish him. She had to believe it would help Julia rest in peace.

“Naahhoooo!” Grimm cried, catching her as she leaped, so that she crashed back down to the dragon.

He had lunged at her from the side and caught her, sending them both plummeting on the opposite side from Stride. An instant later, the dragon’s tail swept across the very spot where they had been standing.

Carol had been saved from being dashed to bloody pieces, but in exchange, she had lost any chance of catching Stride.

The dragon’s three heads howled, oblivious to Carol’s frustration-and then, the creature dove after the walking disaster.

She saw his lips form a single word as he watched the beast approach: “Come.”

Here at the bitter end, he would escape Carol’s blade, giving his life instead to the fangs of the monster he himself had summoned.

An instant before it reached him…

“My looooord!”

A woman leaped into space from the window of the crumbling tower. She was burned so badly that it seemed a miracle she was still alive. It was Melinda, and she clung to her husband as the dragon closed in on him.

Its jaws snapped shut on the two of them, husband and wife vanishing together.

10

The appalling heat of the flames that enveloped the tower roof could be felt even inside the structure.

The hot wave that flooded through the open window ignited the dusty air like a curse, instantly turning the uppermost floor of the spire into a paradise of flames and assaulting Theresia and Melinda, who were still there.

No, that wasn’t quite right. The flames only assailed one of them in that upper room.

Melinda shoved Theresia out of the chamber and slammed the iron door to the stairs shut with her whole body, leaving herself in the flame-riddled space.

The fire mercilessly seared her back.

“Ah! Ahhhhhhhh!”

Theresia could hear the screams of pain even through the door. Covering her belly, she raced back to it, but the door had begun to melt, and her frail arms lacked the strength to pry it open.

“You can’t… Melinda! Melinda! Open the door!” Theresia shouted, pounding on the increasingly hot metal. The room beyond was such an inferno that she could feel it through the barrier. Without some way to protect themselves from the intensity of the heat, no human could…

“Why…? Why would you save me like this?”

“The child…in your belly…bears…no…”

“Melinda!” Theresia cried, her head jerking up when she heard the feeble voice. The warped metal stood implacably between them, separating the two women forever as enemies. “Melinda, listen to me! I can try to give you first aid, so just see if there’s anywhere you might be able to crawl out…”

“I am…the Evil Eye who serves a great man. I am…his wife, howsoever unqualified…” “Melinda?”

She almost sounded like she was talking to herself, but Theresia soon realized: As the Sword Saint, she had walked many battlefields during the civil war and had heard this same tone in the voices she encountered in those places where life and death commingled.

This was the voice of someone bewitched by death, moments before their life expired.

The fire that had come tumbling into the room had burned Melinda’s body so badly that death was all but inevitable. And she had saved Theresia from equally mortal wounds. Reflexively, no doubt unconsciously, following the goodness that was in her heart, she had saved Theresia’s child.

Theresia gritted her teeth and clenched her fist tightly. She had to get back into that room somehow. Even if she couldn’t save Melinda, she couldn’t let the other woman die alone.

No one deserved to die alone.

Theresia hurried toward the rooftop, supporting the weight of her belly as she went. With the way the dragon was rampaging, Theresia was terrified to think what might have happened to Carol, who was still up there. It seemed to take forever to work open the door, which had been warped by the heat of the flames, but finally, Theresia got it ajar and emerged onto the roof.

When she did, the first thing she saw on the roof, still hot with the lingering fury of the flames, was the corpse of a beautiful woman lying there with her eyes closed.

“R…Roswaal…”

Theresia knew at a glance that it was her-and that she would never open those eyes again.

Agony filled Theresia’s heart. Wilhelm and Carol would no doubt mourn her death as well, as she had been an irreplaceable friend to them.

Then she gasped and said, “The black dragon!” There was no time to follow the grief in her heart, for there was the black dragon, beating its wings and circling in the sky at this level of the spire’s roof. She could just make out several figures on its back. At length, one of them, someone in black, slipped from the dragon, falling down, down…

“My loooooord!”

At that instant, a shout echoed through the air, and a woman with ashen hair plunged from the window of the tower. It was the kind woman, her body swollen and covered in cruel burns: Melinda.

She grabbed hold of Stride as he plummeted through the air, her small body pressing as tightly to him as she could. In her eyes, the ones that had so long been reviled as Evil Eyes, Theresia could see bliss.

Face-to-face with her husband, Melinda took Stride’s hand in hers, and for that single instant, they drew near to each other, like a truly loving couple.

Then the dragon’s three heads howled, and the pair were swallowed up in its great jaws as it dove after them.

The three heads vied with each other to drive their cruel fangs into the couple, tearing them limb from limb. Never mind that the three mouths led to one stomach. It was as if each head was set on bathing its own fangs in blood as the dragon reduced husband and wife to bloody chunks.

“Urgh…”

Theresia fell to her knees. The strength left her, and she couldn’t move her legs. Was it disappointment or relief? Her heart and mind weren’t sure what to do with what she had seen of Melinda’s end.

Theresia had wanted to talk more with her.

If she could have done that, perhaps she might eventually have been able to understand just a fraction of the happiness that she had seen in those Evil Eyes during Melinda’s last moments.

“Lady Theresia…”

She looked up in surprise at the sound of her name-and saw Carol. The other woman knelt and laid a hand gently on Theresia’s cheek. Theresia placed her hand over it, feeling its warmth, and when she saw that Carol had indeed regained her free will, she wept.

“Carol…Carol, you’re all right?”

“Yes, milady. Thanks to Grimm and…and Julia.”

“Julia…”

Theresia didn’t recognize that name, but Carol’s eyes showed her. When she spoke it, they filled with a profound love and sadness.

Roswaal J Mathers-the woman Carol called Julia-had enabled Carol and Theresia to meet again as they did now.

“Laay T’rsha,” came another voice.

“Grimm… Oh, Grimm, I’m so sorry. I put a terrible burden on you. And where’s Wilhelm?”

“He’th…fighthing,” said Grimm, standing beside Carol, and Theresia closed her eyes.

Wilhelm was fighting. Yes, of course, of course he was. Wilhelm was always fighting. Always wielding his sword, always battling to protect something.

So, of course, at this moment, his battle went on.

“The leaders of Stride’s faction are dead,” Carol said. “But the black dragon…”

“We can only hope it will go back where it came from without wreaking any more havoc,” Theresia replied.

The Holy Dragon Volcanica was said to be a wise, intelligent, and compassionate being, but even Lugunica, called the Dragonfriend Kingdom, had no record of an actual encounter with any dragon other than Volcanica. This black dragon looked like it was about to rewrite the legends.

Then Carol gasped and pointed to the sky. “Look! The dragon!”

Once it was done chewing the foul fiend and his wife, the dragon spread its wings and rose high into the sky above the city. If only it would flap its wings and head back toward the great waterfall that was held to be the dragons’ home.

It was a slim hope. And it soon proved vain, annihilated by the heat rays emitted as each of the dragon’s heads faced in a different direction and roared.

Waves of devastating heat ran roughshod over the city, causing the streets to erupt in flames as they passed. Uninhabited buildings exploded, further spreading the conflagration. Cries could be heard all over the city.

“The city! Hngh… Is the dragon still enraged?!” Carol exclaimed.

“Those voices…is ev’yone…sane again?” Grimm said. Each had their own reaction to the destruction wrought by the dragon: Carol to the creature’s anger, Grimm to the screams from the streets.

Theresia, for her part, opened her eyes wide. “Wilhelm!”

As the three-headed dragon perched high in the sky, black wings outspread, a bolt of silver light flashed toward it. It was a stroke from Wilhelm van Astrea, the Sword Devil, driving at the black dragon.

The dragon bellowed again, roaring at this unexpected attack delivered by a puny creature who should never have been able to reach the sky. Wilhelm’s swing did inflict damage on the dragon, a superficial wound to its wings.

“Just how far can that man…?” Carol watched Wilhelm attack the dragon as if she couldn’t believe her eyes.

Beside her, Grimm gave a somewhat pained smile. Then he turned to

Theresia. “Yoh two…ge’ out ah here.” “Grimm?” she said.

His gaze was fixed on Theresia’s belly. Only then did she realize she hadn’t removed her hands from her stomach since she had laid eyes on the dragon. Almost of their own accord, they offered the child in her womb a gentle touch, to reassure it.

In Carol’s eyes there was a flicker of hesitation. She could still fight, so shouldn’t she? “Grimm, I-oh!”

He silenced her objection by drawing her close and pressing his lips to hers.

Sweet, delicate, their lips touched. Carol stiffened in surprise-then, as Grimm gently released her, she flushed bright red and said, “Wha… Wha, wha, wha…”

“Ah’m leafing the life of th’ people ah love in your hands.”

“Y… Yes, I understand. Grimm, just, please…be safe.” Carol’s hesitation had melted away on her lips. She placed her hands on his chest as if in prayer. Grimm, accepting what was in her heart, nodded firmly at Theresia. His eyes were filled with certainty and determination, and Theresia made no move to stop him.

“Ah won’t le’ him figh’ alone,” Grimm said.

“Then go, Grimm Fauzen,” Theresia replied. “Knight of the Shield. The Sword Saint, Theresia van Astrea, bears witness to your resolve.”

“I will.”

Grimm accepted Theresia’s words as a blessing and nodded deeply, his face shining.

Then he turned his back to both of them, looked up at the twilight sky where the Sword Devil was waging an awesome battle against the black dragon, and bellowed: “Hrrooooohhh!”

With his great shield on his back, he jumped from the spire rooftop to a nearby building. From there, he jumped down to ground level, never breaking his stride, and raced toward where his brother was fighting.

Watching him go, Carol gently lifted Roswaal’s body in her arms. When she looked back at Theresia, all the anxiety and sorrow were gone from her eyes.

Theresia nodded, firm and strong.

“Lady Theresia,” Carol said, “let’s go.”

“Yes. Let’s do what we were meant to do. Let’s make the people who love us proud.”

11

Taking a short step back in time to the moment just before the Sword Devil launched himself at the black dragon…

“So…the Evil Eye’s spell has been broken.”

A terrifying cleaver came down on Wilhelm, but he parried, then landed a glancing blow on his opponent’s massive chest. Eight-Arms, bare and blue, took a step back and muttered those words in a grave voice.

Only out of the corner of his eye did Wilhelm see the significance of the words. He gritted his teeth and gave a great snort.

Just at the edges of his vision, Pictat’s city guards were dropping their weapons and looking at each other, befuddled. They had been under the control of the Evil Eye, used as pawns to force Zergev Squadron to fight their own countrymen-but now, they were free and had come back to themselves.

“Give it everything, Wilhelm! Leave the rest to us!” cried Bordeaux, and the squadron raised their blades aloft and shouted their approval. Then they started calling out to the confused guards, trying to get away from the battlefield as fast as they could.

Observing Bordeaux’s faultless command, Kurgan smiled, looking like a grinning cliffside. “Virtuosic. A fine soldier. Your men are well drilled.”

“Yeah, well, their captain is the least reliable of any of them. So he’d better have a firm foundation under him.”

“You jest. But if the Evil Eye’s control has been shattered…”

Kurgan was interrupted by the dragon’s roar cascading down from overhead. They looked up to see the three-headed monster writhe in the sky- something was stuck to it.

There were, in fact, several someones up there, fighting on the dragon’s back, of all places. They must be absolute idiots.

“And I’ve gotta go back up those fools. Time for you to give up and die,” Wilhelm said.

“I regret to inform you that you are not the only one with an idiot to support. You do not have a monopoly on foolishness.”

As they went back and forth, their swords flashed white, blade and cleaver meeting once again.

Wilhelm springboarded from the ground and off the walls, using the entire city while Kurgan wielded his eight arms and four cleavers like a raging storm.

Throughout the fight, Wilhelm found himself wondering over and over: Why would this man have joined forces with Stride?

Was it because of his burning desire to test himself in battle against the strongest foes? That would be too shallow a reason.

Wilhelm would not have gone so far as to say that when you matched swords, you understood someone else’s humanity, but there were certain things dueling indeed conveyed to you. The way of life Wilhelm found in Eight-Arms’s blades was not that of a cheap assassin.

“But then again, it doesn’t seem like he’s being controlled by the rings, either.”

In Kurgan’s sword work was none of the hesitation or pause of someone acting under compulsion. For that matter, the interaction between Stride and Kurgan seemed most unlike that of a master and his servant. Kurgan chided Stride about his attitude, advised and cautioned him, and ultimately lent him his strength, as he did now. If anything, the way he acted with Stride seemed almost like…

“Father and child? Is that what you are?” Wilhelm demanded, even as he spun like a top, delivering an innumerable series of blows.

“Not by blood, no,” said Kurgan, blocking the ultra-quick strikes, sparks flying everywhere.

Stride and Kurgan’s relationship was that of a child and parent not related by blood-so had one raised the other?

“Sorry to have to tell you this, but your parentingsucks,” Wilhelm said.

“You will hear no objection from me. I would offer the wish that you not repeat my own mistakes, but sadly, you may not live to behold the face of your child.”

“Keep yapping!” Wilhelm snapped, and the speed of his blows grew even faster. As Kurgan turned his cleaver sidelong to catch them, his eyes widened the slightest bit. Cracks began to appear in the Devil Cleavers.

It was the proof that Wilhelm had landed blow after inch-perfect blow on the same spot-and an instant later, the Sword Devil’s terrible blade finally shattered one of Eight-Arms’s cherished weapons.

The eight arms and four cleavers had offered an all but impenetrable defense, but now, the momentum of the battle shifted.

Wilhelm, he who had defeated the Sword Saint, stepped in to end the duel in one quick stroke.

“Devil Cleaver!”

At that exact moment, a chill he had never felt before gripped his entire body.

Before him, Kurgan spread his eight arms up and down, left and right, each of the three remaining Devil Cleavers arcing at Wilhelm three different directions, the free hands each grabbing a blade and pulling back, acting as a sort of fulcrum. This restraining force generated a massive amount of latent energy crying out for release. And when it was unleashed, unimaginable power would come hurtling from three directions.

“Can you dodgethis, Sword Devil?”

It was a letter of challenge, thrust upon him. If Wilhelm avoided the strike, victory was his; if not, he would lose. The Sword Devil gritted his teeth.

The war god launched death upon him from three sides, each streaking in like a comet.

12

Let us digress a moment to speak of a certain father and son.

The succession to the throne of the Holy Volakian Empire was determined via a ritual known as the Rite of Imperial Selection, in which the various claimants killed each other until only one remained.

Stride Volakia was among those destined to take part in this succession dispute.

It was not so complicated as to how Stride ended up in Kurgan’s care. Stride’s family had recognized their son’s physical weakness from an early age and had given him to another household on the condition the boy give up his claim to the throne. The household that accepted him sent him to Kurgan with a request that he be trained.

Disgraced he may have been, but Stride was still Volakian royalty. An overt assassination would be inappropriate. But if he happened to die under Kurgan’s severe tutelage, so be it. Stride, however, survived.

Stride used his inborn greed and powers of observation to foil the hopes of a great many people, and indeed, even to show he had the mettle to stand among those who would fight for the throne.

With no one to vouch for him, however, he would never be part of the battle.

Poisoned, Stride spent three days and three nights vomiting blood. Seven days and seven nights, he hovered between life and death, then for three full months, he was lost between dreams and reality. When the poison finally receded…

“Hear me, Kurgan. In the throes of my fever, I saw the truth. I saw the beings seated in the heavens who look down on us and laugh-the observers who play with us like pawns in a game.”

Stride was thinner and more wasted than ever. He had become like a man half dead. Yet in his eyes burned an ambition for the throne far greater than he had ever shown before, and this was what caused Kurgan to choose the path he had.

“However foolish the road that you choose to walk, Stride, you are my son. I cannot obey an empire that tells my child not to live but to die.”

This foolish, isolated son of his, unable to love anyone-though there be no one else, Kurgan at least would love him.

At the bitter end, Kurgan suspected, this man would be consumed by the flames of hatred and fury, his corpse abused by all and sundry, his way of life cruelly rejected.

Kurgan had done all this. He would do all this. He had no intention of dissuading Stride from his plans. If Stride was going to take the road of death, then Kurgan would walk it with him.

That was love, so far as a father sometimes called the very god of war could show to his foolish, cherished son.

As death hurtled toward him like three comets, the Sword Devil delivered an answer that was simplicity itself.

If inevitable death was closing upon him, he merely needed to make sure the steel in his hand was faster yet.

He surpassed high-speed to hyperspeed, then hyperspeed to godlike speed, until his sword became a force that transcended the very notion of steel.

Above, left, right. He did not know what feeling entered Eight-Arms’s heart in the moment Wilhelm blocked the three blows head-on.

In that moment, even Wilhelm himself did not comprehend how extraordinary his deflections had been. It may have been not a whit less impressive than when he had defeated Theresia van Astrea, the Sword Saint, at the ceremony marking the conclusion of the Demi-human War. In other words, it was a move that transcended even the Sword Saint… “Once…there was a man who had mastered the blade,” said Kurgan.

Wilhelm said nothing.

“His sword work was beautiful, brutal, tranquil, ferocious, and strong beyond measure.”

It was a story that had enraptured a great many who lived by the sword in this world. If envy of the Sword Saint was infatuation with pure skill, then the

name of the utter mastery of technique was…

“Have you set foot upon the stair to the Heavenly Blade?”

“What are you, talking in your sleep? The hell do I care about the

Heavenly Blade?”

Wilhelm clucked his tongue and put his sword back in its scabbard. Then he turned and saw Kurgan, his eight arms hanging limply at his sides, all function lost, and a deep wound running from his chest to his belly.

The cleavers he had dropped dug into the ground, and as he stood amid them, the god of war smiled. “Magnificent.”

Kurgan spoke only that one, brief word, and then blood poured from his lips. His great form crumpled to its knees, and he pitched forward with a thud. Wilhelm watched him, then heaved a great sigh. “I managed, somehow.

You were one hell of an opponent…” “Wilhelm!”

After the life-or-death struggle with this man, there was no glow of victory. Instead, Wilhelm struggled with an overwhelming fatigue-but Conwood ran up to him, looking amazed.

“Incredible! You beat Volakia’s Eight-Arms? You really are a-”

“Not the time, Conwood. This battle isn’t over. Where are the city guards?”

“Bordeaux’s got the uninjured and only lightly hurt folks helping to move the seriously wounded. We tried to fight a defensive battle, but there were still a lot of casualties.”

“I’m worried about where Grimm and Roswaal went running off to. More than anything else, really.”

When he looked up, he could see a change in the black dragon that had been circling the spire above them. Its three heads seemed to be fighting over something, then the creature shot into the sky. Wilhelm would have been more than happy to see it fly off into the distance, but evidently, this would not end so easily.

The rampaging dragon stretched out its heads, and each began to breathe fire in a different direction. The city was incinerated, the streets filled with the screams of people overcome by the great white light, and the dragon roared.

“Guess it’s not very happy about being summoned here by someone who didn’t know any manners. If we don’t stop that thing, it’s only a matter of time until the kingdom is destroyed,” Wilhelm said. As Conwood looked on, aghast, Wilhelm slowly turned toward the monster.

“W-wait, Wilhelm!” Conwood exclaimed. “You’re not…you’re not really going to fight that thing, are you?!”

“What? You don’t think someone from the Dragonfriend Kingdom should go around slicing up dragons?”

“Not what I’m worried about! But…do battle with that creature?!”

Conwood couldn’t bring himself to say outright that it was hopeless. Not with the deep blue eyes that Wilhelm turned and fixed on him.

“Conwood, go back to the rest of the squad and make sure the citizens get out of here. Our messenger should be able to bring the reinforcements by the time you’re done. With the kingdom’s entire strength, we can fillet that overgrown lizard.”

Wilhelm made no mention of whether it was actually possible. He had spoken, and he would do what he had said.

Conwood, therefore, paused to take several breaths, then nodded, just once. “Don’t you die before you even get to see your kid’s face, Wilhelm,” he said.

“Speaking of which, try to find my wife for me. This doesn’t look like something I’m going to be able to fight while I’m looking for my woman at the same time.”

With that, Wilhelm was off like a shot.

He had no idea how much of the dragon’s behavior was at Stride’s instigation. He ground his teeth. The villain must have some goal beyond simply unleashing the beast on the kingdom.

He kicked off the brutalized street, raced up the wall of a building scorched by flames, jumped from one charred rooftop to the next, and raised his sword against the dragon where it floated in a sky now bathed in twilight.

“Yaaaaaahhhh!”

The dragon was probably hardly aware of him, a trivial being offering trivial resistance.

The silver flash of the Sword Devil stabbed through the creature’s awful, beautiful wing.

13

Run, run, and then keep running, as fast as you can.

Grimm Fauzen dashed for all he was worth through the city-turnedbattlefield.

The heat rays scoured the town at large, with no single target. As the great white light scorched everything in every direction, leaving Pictat enveloped in crimson flames, the place became a vision of hell, where every breath left ash in his mouth.

The twilight from the sky and the quavering flames from the earth conspired to turn the whole world a burning red.

The dragon roared in the sky, and people cried out on the ground, but as for Grimm, he raced toward the sound of ringing steel.

“Ill…elm…!”

The battle unfolding above him at that moment was almost beyond the bounds of human imagining.

How could Wilhelm think he could fight a supernatural creature like a dragon-winged, vastly larger than any human, with scales stronger than steel? Could a puny human ever hope to stand alone against such a beast? Who could blame a person for dropping their sword in fear and running away, weeping?

And yet, Grimm went. He raced for the fight that could not be fought alone.

“…Ait…fo’ me!”

I’m coming. I’m coming right now. I will reach you.

I won’t let you fight alone. I swear it.

“Yaaaaaahhhh!”

He brought down the sacred blade, parried the dragon’s claws, which sought to sweep him away, with all his might. His shoulders groaned under the impact, and his muscles tore. He felt the blow all the way through his gritted teeth.

Feeble! His blow was too light-his sword far too dull.

He had to remember his battle with Kurgan. Had to get as close as he could to that instant when he had dodged Kurgan’s killing blow. Or else…or else, the sword work he had pulled off when he had taken Theresia from the Sword God. He had to return to that realm.

There was another tremendous roar, and Wilhelm, who had landed back on the spire, felt his whole body shake with the noise.

The dragon’s tail lashed out, hoping to squash Wilhelm like a bug where he had stopped. Wilhelm, however, used the tail as a ramp to get up and onto the creature’s back.

“Ngggghhh!”

He drove his sword into the tip of the tail and dragged it with him as he went, a spray of blood following him as if in pursuit. Apparently, dragons bled red like everyone else. In the end, they were ordinary living beings-so would a dragon die if you pierced its heart?

“Seems like too much work to cut off your heads, after all!”

The dragon gave a furious cry, and one of its heads bared its fangs at Wilhelm. If it got hold of him, it would tear him apart. The instant he stopped moving would be the instant he died.

He met the oncoming fangs with his sword, bouncing back and carrying the momentum directly into his next move. Another of the heads came at him from a different direction, trying to stop him. Sensing the aura of death from behind him, Wilhelm put all his strength into his arms, still targeting the head in front of him. He paid no heed at all to the attack from behind. And why?

“Grimm!!”

“Gaaaaahhh!”

Because in response to the cry from his old comrade-in-arms, Grimm clambered onto the dragon’s back and blocked the fangs with his great shield.

This enemy struck harder than any human could withstand. The moment he took the blow, Grimm’s knees folded from the impact and snapped audibly. Grimm bit his tongue hard to hold back a scream.

“Wilheeem!!”

When he heard his comrade-in-arm’s impassioned cry, Wilhelm drove again at the dragon. The flash of his sword slid along its fangs, pushing the head aside and cleaving the jaws down the middle. Caught up in the rush of wind from his blade, the dragon’s fangs went flying, trailing blood that spattered across the Sword Devil and made him even redder than before.

Thrashing with the pain of having its face eviscerated, the dragon howled and went into a fast midair spin. Wilhelm and Grimm were thrown back by the force, launched into empty space.

With his knees broken, Grimm had no hope of landing in one piece. Wilhelm kicked off a wall and threw himself after Grimm, grabbing his arm and just managing to roll them both safely to a landing on another nearby building.

“Gah! You…freakin’ idiot… There’s stupid…and then, there’s… stupid…!”

“Huff… huff…Don’ wan’ hear i’…fromyou,” Grimm said in his raspy voice, eliciting, of all things, a smile from Wilhelm. Then they looked up, where the black dragon continued to howl with rage.

Wilhelm narrowed his blue eyes and clucked his tongue. “He just doesn’t know when to give up, does he?”

“-?”

At those words, a question mingled with the pain on Grimm’s face.

Wilhelm let out a quick sigh, then pointed his beloved blade firmly at the dragon hovering above them. “You saw his shit fighting. No way that’s how a dragon really does battle. That’s how anamateurfights.”

“Y’…mean…”

“That’s not the dragon at all… It’sStride.”

Grimm was simply lost for words at that, naturally. Even Wilhelm didn’t have any precise proof of his declaration. It was just his intuition at work. He suspected the power known as the Ten Proud Commandments was actually Stride’s own; the rings were merely catalysts. And here, at the eleventh hour, he was using it to control the most terrible of puppets.

“Worst case scenario, I guess maybe if we kill the caster, Stride, the spell might break…”

“…Can’t. He’s dea’.”

“Yeah… Kinda thought that might be the case,” Wilhelm said, gritting his teeth. In exchange for his own life, Stride had taken away the kingdom’s one hope of stopping the black dragon. To the bitter end, everything seemed to be in the palm of his hand.

Grimm lay looking up, his knees a mess. If he tried to do any more, his legs might never work again.

It would take time for the reinforcements to arrive, and Bordeaux and the others had their hands full evacuating the citizens. And there was no sign of Roswaal. This was going to be a tough fight indeed.

There was no way she was just off somewhere hiding, saving her own neck. She wasn’t that kind of woman.

How much damage can I actually do to this thing on my own?

“Willlelm,” Grimm said, studying him.

At his name, Wilhelm looked at Grimm once more and gasped-because of the expression on his face.

“You’re not…alone.”

The words brimmed with confidence and certainty.

As the city burned with the dragon’s fire, Wilhelm heard voices. He looked up, and his eyes went wide. There were people all throughout Pictat, in every corner of the city, shouting, raising their swords to the sky, and looking in fury at the black dragon.

These people, who had been broken by the thunder of the dragon’s voice, who had seen their city razed by its breath, who had been laid low at every turn, now joined as one and, like Wilhelm in his lonely fight, raised their voices.

Leading them was Zergev Squadron. Conwood stood in the van, flying the flag, and beside him was…

“Theresia!”

Carol stood next to her, supporting her, but Theresia was unmissable, red hair flapping in the hot wind.

Visibly pregnant, her belly protruding mightily, nonetheless she stood at the head of the kingdom’s most valiant men and women with her head held high. It was her voice that had spoken to the people’s hearts, had gathered up the shattered pieces of their souls, and allowed them now to stand tall.

He saw her lips move, there at the head of her formation: “Wilhelm.” Only he immediately understood she had called to him.

She carried no sword but stood before them as a mother, the Sword Saint inspiring her people.

Goddamn, did I pick a good wife, he thought.

The black dragon’s three heads howled once more-but not one person in the crowd was cowed. No spirit was broken; no one even looked down.

Confronted with such defiance, the dragon in the sky forgot its pain and began to tremble with rage. The three heads began to build up flame, ready to wipe out all the heroes on the ground.

Until…

“What are you doing tomywoman?!”

One head was pierced from below by the holy blade, preventing it from expelling its breath.

One head found its jaws crushed by a great shield, forcing the wave of heat back down its own throat, where it exploded.

One head was unable to account for its mutilated jaws, the fire spiraling off toward the dragon’s own wings.

“Yaaaaahhh!”

There was a tremendous explosion in midair, and with a bellow, the dragon fell toward the spire. At the same time, the Sword Devil plummeted, half ablaze.

Wilhelm, having done tremendous damage to the dragon, hurtled back down to earth. If he’d hit it, he would have died on the spot. But he didn’t.

“I don’t know how many times you would’ve died without me, you great idiot.”

He was caught by a pair of hulking, steady arms. Wilhelm forced his eyes to open in spite of the pain, and he was met with the sight of a man wearing a brave smile: Bordeaux.

Seeing that grin close up, Wilhelm couldn’t help flashing a wry smile himself. “I’ve never seen timing quite like that,” he said. “How’d you know exactly where I was going to fall?”

“You’re gonna laugh…but a familiar voice said to me, ‘Young man, go and catch him.’”

Wilhelm was struck dumb.

“That’s why I was on time. I’m not sure if it was a phantasm from the past or daydream or what, but whatever the case, it sure came in handy.”

At that, Wilhelm closed his eyes. He didn’t hear the voice anymore. It had been the symbol of his regret, the proof he was still in the grip of the Evil Eye. It was impossible that product of his delusion should somehow affect actual reality.

Yet without at least that much of a miracle, he wouldn’t be alive at this moment.

“You fought through, and you did good. You won this one,” Bordeaux said.

“Don’t get ahead of yourself, moron,” Wilhelm shot back, his breath coming hard as he hopped out of Bordeaux’s arms. “That dragon’s not dead yet.”

Bordeaux, however, shook his head. “That’s where you’re wrong. This fight is over. His Majesty is on the move.”

“His Majesty Jionis?” Wilhelm knitted his brow at a name he’d never expected to hear at this moment.

Jionis Lugunica, of the Kingdom of Lugunica: Wilhelm was well acquainted with the depth of his decency but had trouble imagining the king as the keystone to this battle. Surely, he wouldn’t take up arms himself and come here to strike down the dragon with his own hand?

The next moment, though, Wilhelm’s breath caught. The reason was shock, and the source of the shock his own actions.

At some point, without even realizing it, Wilhelm had knelt and bowed his head.

He looked over and saw that Bordeaux, beside him, had done the same. He could feel on his skin that every other person there had done likewise. Silence hung over the city. The gallant voices so recently raised in defiance of the dragon’s roars had vanished. No one spoke, but all naturally bowed.

For it was…

“In accordance with the ancient pact, for the sake of the children of the Lion King, on these wings I have come.”

For it was the Holy Dragon, a resplendent blue, floating in the sky with the reddening evening sun behind it.

Every being in the city had knelt at the shock of the voice, which seemed to whisper directly to their souls. There could be no thought of defiance in its presence, but only a natural instinct to bend the knee in awe at this overwhelming presence.

Wilhelm found his mind had gone blank, his throat was frozen with amazement, and his five senses had all but stopped functioning. Within him, there was only utter awe at this absolute creature, whose name everyone in the kingdom knew.

This was the noble being who had made a pact with the Dragonfriend Kingdom of Lugunica, a true dragon if ever there was one.

“I am Volcanica. My old friend’s blood has cried out to me, and thus here

I appear.”

By its advent on its wings, the Holy Dragon Volcanica settled all matters.

As everyone on the awestruck battlefield continued to kneel, the silence that reigned over the world was abruptly interrupted by a barbarous noise of destruction. It came from the spire, where the three-headed black dragon had attempted to haul up its huge body, and in so doing had dealt the final blow to the stone tower.

The awe gripped the black dragon as well. It feared Volcanica as a being it could not resist. How very small it looked before the Holy Dragon. Pitifully weak and mild. Even as everyone refrained from looking directly at the creatures, the difference was clear.

The black dragon howled once more. It had to instinctively understand the hopelessness of its position, but still it was not brought to heel. The fury of battle came into its six eyes, and it spread its wings before the Holy Dragon. It gave a cry, its voice echoing around Pictat’s twilit streets.

Was it Wilhelm’s imagination, or did it sound like a cry of joy?

“Oh, pitiful Bargren. You have lost your beloved child, and your dragonskin has fallen into evil.”Volcanica’s voice was heartrending, overflowing with nothing but compassion. Its body was covered in scales that shimmered a bluish white and was many times larger than the black dragon it called Bargren. Volcanica was a dragon in the truest sense of the word.

Its eyes were wise, it had the knowledge to know human language better than humans themselves, and its whole body was ensconced in dense mana. The very sky around it warped, the flames on the ground were purified, and the world that should have been burned was healed.

Indeed, the healing the dragon bestowed did not stop there.

“Unbelievable…”

Astonished, Wilhelm looked down at his own body, watching wide-eyed as the wounds he had sustained on this battlefield healed themselves. Beside him, Bordeaux saw the same, as did Grimm on top of the building.

He assumed the Holy Dragon’s blessing was being poured out upon the whole city. Those who had been injured here, hanging between life and death, were revived, and they looked up to the heavens at this miracle.

And itwasa miracle, bestowed by the dragon, though everyone said that the pact had been abandoned, that the Holy Dragon would not come to help the kingdom in its time of need.

“Sleep in peace, O friend of mine. Your way has been twisted.”

To the Holy Dragon’s richly tender voice, the black dragon answered with a cruel howl. The battle with the Sword Devil had left Bargren’s heads savagely mutilated, but all three of them looked up to the sky and breathed in, ready to exhale again.

The Holy Dragon regarded Bargren with sadness, then flapped its wings, sinking down to the black dragon’s level. Did the other dragon realize that was a mark of care, so that the fire Volcanica breathed would not land on the city?

They would never know the answer.

The black dragon roared once more, white light lancing from all three of its mouths at once. The bright spears joined into a single beam of heat, a wave of destruction aimed at Volcanica.

Volcanica faced it head-on and opened its mouth.

Blue light filled the sky, striking down the oncoming white beam without even giving it time to resist.

Doing no damage to anything between the Holy Dragon and its target, Volcanica’s breath enveloped the black dragon’s body, reducing it to dust. It was not a cruel death, but an end brought by the power of what might be called purification. The black dragon, which had been snared by evil and forced into a battle it did not wish to fight, was erased from existence by the Holy Dragon’s breath.

Then the intense, sacred light cleared, and the black dragon was nowhere to be seen.
